## 23. Terminal titles and bell indicators (`23-terminal-titles-and-bell.md`)

Two QOL surface enhancements on top of §22. (1) **Title-change escapes:** `term.onTitleChange` is wired so OSC 0 / OSC 2 (`\x1b]0;TITLE\x07`) updates `runtimeTitle` on the `TerminalInstance`, and the drawer tab + in-pane header label resolve to it via `effectiveTabLabel`. Falls back to the configured `name` (or derived basename) when the runtime title is empty; resets on PTY restart and on project switch. (2) **Bell indicator (Phase 1):** `term.onBell` sets `hasBell` on the `TerminalInstance`; when the firing terminal isn't the active drawer tab, a Lucide `bell` glyph wiggles into place next to the tab label and clears as soon as the tab is activated. The bell-during-active case is suppressed by an `isTerminalTabActive` guard. **Phase 2** is specified separately in §24.

**Status:** Shipped Phase 1 — title escapes (full) + same-project bell indicator. Implementation in `src/client/terminal.tsx` (`runtimeTitle`, `hasBell`, `effectiveTabLabel`, `BELL_ICON`, `updateTabLabel`) and `src/client/styles.scss` (`.drawer-tab-bell` + `drawer-tab-bell-shake` keyframe). Cross-refs: §22 (base terminal feature), §24 (Phase 2 spec).

---

## 24. Cross-project bell indicator (`24-cross-project-bell.md`)

Phase 2 of the bell indicator: surface bells fired in non-current projects (where no client xterm is mounted) and in not-yet-mounted terminals within a project. Server-side `\x07` detection is added to the `TerminalRegistry` PTY data handler, setting a per-session `bellPending: boolean` flag that survives until explicitly cleared. New endpoints: `POST /api/terminal/clear-bell` (acknowledge + clear), `GET /api/projects/bell-state` (cross-project long-poll mirroring `/api/projects/permissions`), and an extended `/api/terminal/list` that includes `bellPending` per session. Client gains a `src/client/bellPoll.tsx` long-poll loop that updates a per-project bell map and re-renders both the project-tab indicator (suppressed on the active project, shown on others) and the in-drawer per-terminal indicators. Activating a project hides the project-tab indicator without clearing per-terminal flags, so the user can still see which specific terminal wanted attention. Activating a terminal tab clears its server-side `bellPending`. In-memory only — server restart drops all pending bells (intentional). No new user settings in v1; possible follow-ups call out an audio chime, decay timer, and full suppression toggle.

**Status:** Shipped. Server-side: `TerminalRegistry`'s PTY data handler flips a per-session `bellPending` flag on `0x07`; helpers (`getBellPending`, `clearBellPending`, `listBellPendingForProject`) are exposed to the route layer. `/api/terminal/list` now includes `bellPending` per entry; `/api/terminal/clear-bell` clears the flag; `/api/projects/bell-state` long-poll aggregates pending state across every registered project. Client-side: `src/client/bellPoll.tsx` runs the long-poll loop from app boot, populates a module-level `BellStateMap`, and fans out via `updateProjectBellIndicators` in `projectTabs.tsx` (adds `.has-bell` + Lucide bell SVG to non-active project tabs) and a `subscribeToBellState` callback in `terminal.tsx` (syncs in-drawer per-terminal indicators). `loadAndRenderTerminalTabs` seeds `inst.hasBell` from the list response's `bellPending` field; `activateTerminal` fires-and-forgets `/api/terminal/clear-bell` so the server flag drops. In-memory only — server restart clears all pending bells. Cross-refs: §22 (base terminal), §23 (Phase 1).

---

## 25. Terminal dashboard view (`25-terminal-dashboard.md`)

A second top-level client view (alongside the normal per-project ticket view) for eyeballing every terminal across every registered project at once. Entered via a new `square-terminal` toolbar button placed before the first project tab (HS-7030 — was `layout-panel-left`) (shown on web + Tauri since HS-8624 enabled web terminals; was Tauri-only). While active, only the toggle button and the project-tab strip remain visible in the top toolbar — settings, search, layout toggles, channel cluster, ticket area, detail panel, and per-project drawer are all hidden. Content area becomes a vertically scrollable column of per-project sections: project heading, then a flex-wrap grid of 4:3 terminal tiles with the terminal title centered below each tile. Every tile is identically sized — one global computation picks the largest width such that all tiles fit the viewport (min 100 px preview height; content scrolls vertically when even the floor doesn't fit). Tiles render a shared xterm instance pinned at a per-tile cols × rows picked at mount time from measured cell metrics so natural pixel size ≈ 1280 × 960 (matches the 4:3 tile) — typically ~160 × 60 on macOS ui-monospace 13px — and visually fit via `transform: scale(...)` — the PTY is untouched and other attachers (drawer, other windows) see no reflow. Single-click zooms a tile to ~70 % viewport centered overlay with focus + keyboard input; click outside / Esc / click same tile returns to grid; click a different tile swaps. Double-click enters a dedicated full-viewport view that _does_ `fit()` (PTY resized to match) and whose Back/Esc return to the grid. Bells bounce the tile once (350 ms keyframe) and persist an accent outline until the user centers the tile, enters its dedicated view, or exits dashboard and opens the drawer — any of which fires `POST /api/terminal/clear-bell` (reusing §24 transport). Lazy-unspawned and exited terminals render a placeholder tile (label + play glyph + status); spawning happens on enlarge (center or dedicated), not at dashboard open. Projects with zero terminals still render their heading plus an "open Settings → Terminal to add one" empty-state row. Exit paths: click the toggle again, press Esc on the bare grid, or click any project tab (auto-exits dashboard **and** navigates to that project's ticket view). No new server endpoints, no new settings — dashboard-open is an in-memory client-only flag that resets on reload.

**Status:** Shipped v1 + Flow layout mode (HS-7662 / spec HS-7624) + HS-7968 tile virtualization. HS-7968 lazily mounts/disposes each tile's xterm + WebSocket via an `IntersectionObserver` (200 px rootMargin) with an 8 s dispose-debounce — pushes the practical client-side ceiling from "total terminals in the project" to "terminals visible on screen at once" without affecting bell indicators or status dots (both read from `/api/terminal/list` polling, independent of mount state). Pure state machine in `terminalTileVirtualization.ts` (12 unit tests). Click-before-IO race defended via `ensureTileMounted` in `centerTile`. Off-screen tiles re-mount + replay scrollback (server-side PTY + scrollback stay alive). HS-6272 parent and HS-6832 through HS-6838 sub-tickets all completed; HS-7662 ships an alternate flat-grid layout mode persisted via `dashboard_layout_mode: 'sectioned' | 'flow'` in `/file-settings` (default `'sectioned'`), togglable from a new `#terminal-dashboard-layout-toggle` button in the dashboard toolbar. Flow mode dissolves per-project sections into one grid in registered-project order, drops empty projects entirely, and marks each tile with a project-color badge derived from a stable hash of the project secret (HSL hue) — the first tile of each project's run additionally gets a `{ProjectName} ›` label prefix; bell long-poll subscription unions every project's pending IDs into the single flow handle. 4 e2e tests in `e2e/terminal-dashboard-flow-layout.spec.ts` cover toggle visibility + reload persistence, flat-grid rendering with badge / project-prefix counts, no-fetch round-trip on toggle (cached lastSectionData), and empty-projects-dropped behavior. Bug-fix follow-ups: HS-6865 (explicit xterm-root width/height so xterm's internal absolutely-positioned layers have a concrete post-scale box), HS-6866 (share `readXtermTheme()` with the drawer so tile canvases use `--bg` / `--text` / `--accent` instead of xterm's default black), HS-6867 (FLIP grow-from-slot animation with a gray placeholder so centering a tile doesn't reflow the rest of the grid), HS-6868 (suppress the active-tab highlight while dashboard mode is open — global view, no project is "selected"), HS-6898 (non-uniform `scale(scaleX, scaleY)` to fill the 4:3 tile — **superseded by HS-6931**), HS-6931 (uniform `scale(s)` — text no longer stretches; `.xterm-screen` is the authoritative natural-dim measurement source rather than the block-level outer xterm root. The HS-6931 follow-up that resized xterm to a measured-cell 4:3 target (1280 × 960) was **superseded by HS-6965** — force-resetting the xterm back to that target after the history replay caused live bytes formatted for the PTY's own cols × rows to wrap at the wrong column and leave a band of empty rows below the last line of real content. The dedicated view's deferred `fit()` + `ResizeObserver` is retained.), HS-6964 (centered tile preview was sliding off the viewport centre because `tile.style.width` stayed at the grid-slot value while the preview was resized to `previewWidth` — `align-items: center` then flex-centered the larger preview around the smaller tile box. Fix: `centerTile` also sets `tile.style.width = previewWidth`, `applyTileSizing` skips centered tiles on resize, the dashboard's resize handler calls `recenterTile` so the centered overlay tracks the viewport centre, and preview snap writes use `transition: none` so the outer FLIP is the only animation running.), HS-6965 (superseded by HS-7097 follow-up — replay still runs at the PTY's cols × rows so scrollback bytes render correctly, but the tile then resizes its xterm to tile-native 4:3 dims via `tileNativeGridFromCellMetrics` AND pushes a `'resize'` message to the server-side PTY so a running TUI like `nano` actually `SIGWINCH`-redraws to fill the tile-native geometry — without the PTY resize, the tile shows the TUI's content from the original wide-short PTY rows with empty white rows below), HS-6997 (top-align the scaled xterm inside the tile preview — vertical dead space from HS-6965's letterboxing falls below the content in one band, like a macOS Terminal pane whose content hasn't yet reached the bottom, rather than sandwiching the content between equal bands top and bottom; encoded as `top: 0, left: centered` in `computeTileScale()`), HS-7096 (no CSS transition on preview width / height — slider drags and window resizes must snap, not animate, or the xterm transform scales against an intermediate box), HS-7097 (rescale via `.xterm-screen` ResizeObserver — replaces the earlier two-rAF chain that raced xterm's own render scheduler and could still fire against pre-resize `.xterm-screen` dims on first-history-after-mount; follow-up: tile's xterm is pinned to tile-native 4:3 cols × rows via `tileNativeGridFromCellMetrics` after replay + on mount; final follow-up: the tile's history handler also pushes a `'resize'` message to the server-side PTY at tile-native dims so a TUI like `nano` redraws to fill the tile geometry — the buffer-only resize left rows past the PTY's row count empty (visible as the white band on the user's "still wrong" screenshots). `exitDedicatedView()` re-sends the same `'resize'` so the PTY snaps back to the tile's geometry after the dedicated view temporarily took it. E2E coverage in `e2e/terminal-dashboard-tile-rendering.spec.ts` with a real PTY running a Python `SIGWINCH`-redraw fixture asserts the BOTTOM marker sits within 10 % of the preview bottom across all three views.), HS-7098 (`.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-body` keeps `padding: 16px` for the visual frame + xterm opens inside an inner `.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-pane` flex child with NO padding so FitAddon sees real available space; follow-up: pane is a flex container with centering + `.xterm` child has `flex: 0 0 auto` so it shrinks to `.xterm-screen`'s content width — sub-cell slop becomes symmetric left/right padding instead of an asymmetric right-side gap), HS-7099 (REMOVED by HS-7097 follow-up — mirroring the dedicated view's non-4:3 fit dims onto the grid tile re-introduced HS-7097's vertical-dead-space regression; tile now stays on tile-native 4:3 dims through the dedicated-view lifecycle), HS-7129 (slider default 50 → 33 so the dashboard opens with ~three tiles per row on a typical laptop instead of one big tile), HS-7228 (dashboard's per-project `+` button passes `{ spawn: true }` to `POST /api/terminal/create` so the new tile lands as a live preview rather than a cold `not_spawned` placeholder — the drawer's `+` gets eager-spawn for free because it selects the new tab (which attaches a WS and triggers the spawn), but the dashboard has no such follow-up attach; `spawn: true` makes the server call `ensureSpawned(..., configOverride)` synchronously during /create — see §25.4 for the documented "cold tiles stay cold" exception). Out of scope for v1 (deferred): keyboard shortcut to toggle, drag-to-reorder tiles, per-tile lifecycle buttons, input into grid tiles, resizable centered overlay, persisted dashboard-open state, multi-select, audio bell. Cross-refs: §22 (base terminal), §23 (bell Phase 1 — same concept at tile granularity), §24 (bell-state long-poll reused verbatim), §4 (top toolbar chrome that gets hidden), §10 (Tauri-only gating pattern).

---

## 29. OSC 7 shell CWD tracking (`29-osc7-cwd-tracking.md`)

HS-7262. Shells emit `\x1b]7;file://host/path\x07` on every prompt (starship, zsh `chpwd`, fish, VS Code integration, iTerm2, Apple Terminal). Before this change the bell scanner specifically silenced the terminator (HS-6766) but discarded the payload. Now the drawer terminal registers a `term.parser.registerOscHandler(7, ...)` hook that parses the `file://host/path` URL, URL-decodes the path, and stores it on `TerminalInstance.runtimeCwd`. A **CWD chip** in the in-pane toolbar (hidden until the shell pushes its first OSC 7) shows a truncated path with a folder glyph; clicking POSTs to the new `/api/terminal/open-cwd` endpoint which validates existence + directory-ness before dispatching to the existing cross-platform `openInFileManager` helper (reused from project-reveal).

Pure helpers `parseOsc7Payload` + `formatCwdLabel` extracted into `src/client/terminalOsc7.ts` with 16 unit tests. Server endpoint has 5 unit tests in `api.test.ts` covering the 400/404/directory-check paths. `runtimeCwd` resets to null on PTY restart and on project switch (mirrors `runtimeTitle` §23.2). `$HOME` is unknown on the client for v1 so tildification is disabled (parser accepts home arg and has full tildify test coverage — just the plumbing is missing); follow-up **HS-7276** adds `$HOME` to `/terminal/list` response. Other follow-ups: **HS-7277** dashboard `+` inherits active tile CWD, **HS-7278** server-side OSC 7 tracking + dashboard tile CWD badge.

**Status:** Shipped v1.

---

## 28. OSC 8 clickable hyperlinks (`28-osc8-hyperlinks.md`)

HS-7263. xterm.js's `linkHandler` constructor option routes activation of OSC 8 hyperlinks (`\x1b]8;;URL\x07TEXT\x1b]8;;\x07`) through a new shared `openExternalUrl` helper in `tauriIntegration.tsx` that invokes the `open_url` Tauri command and falls back to `window.open` in browser builds. Applied to the drawer terminal (`terminal.tsx mountXterm`) and both dashboard xterms (`terminalDashboard.tsx mountTileXterm` + `openDedicatedView`). The same change updates `WebLinksAddon` instances to pass the custom click handler instead of relying on the default `window.open` — plain-URL click was a silent no-op in WKWebView, a latent pre-existing Tauri bug that HS-7263 incidentally fixes. `bindExternalLinkHandler` (global `<a>` interceptor) refactored to call the new helper. Non-http protocols, hover tooltips, click-through safety prompts: explicitly out of scope. HS-7274 shipped Playwright coverage in `e2e/terminal-drawer-osc8.spec.ts` + `e2e/fixtures/terminal-osc8.sh`: the fixture prints an OSC 8 wrapped text + a bare plain URL, the spec stubs `window.__TAURI__.core.invoke` pre-bundle into a call-capture array, clicks each run, and asserts `invoke('open_url', { url })` fired with the wrapped URL then the plain URL (plain-URL assertion is the regression for the WKWebView-silent-no-op path).

**Status:** Shipped — applied to every xterm in the client, plus the global link interceptor consolidated around the same helper.

---

## 27. OSC 9 desktop notifications (`27-osc9-desktop-notifications.md`)

HS-7264. Shells emit `\x1b]9;<message>\x07` (iTerm2 convention) to surface a human-readable "Build done" / "Tests passed" style message. Hot Sheet treats it as an extension of the bell indicator (§23.3): the message is stashed in `SessionState.notificationMessage`, `bellPending` flips alongside it, and the shared toast helper (`src/client/toast.tsx`, extracted from pluginUI) renders it for **6 s** (vs. 3 s for plugin-action toasts). Scanner implementation: the existing OSC-aware bell scanner (HS-6766) now also accumulates OSC payloads into `oscAccumulator` (capped at 4 KiB) while inside an OSC specifically (not DCS/APC/PM/SOS), and on terminator inspects for `9;<message>`. Numeric-subcommand forms (`9;1;…`, `9;4;…`, iTerm2 proprietary progress) are parked — not worth spamming toasts for.

Transport: `/api/projects/bell-state` long-poll payload gains `notifications: Record<terminalId, string>` alongside `terminalIds`; `/api/terminal/list` entries gain `notificationMessage: string | null`. `clearBellPending` drops both fields atomically.

Scope: toasts fire for the **active project only** — cross-project OSC 9 surfaces as a project-tab bell dot, and the message toast appears when the user switches to that project (via `loadAndRenderTerminalTabs` → `fireToastsForActiveProject`). Dedupe cache (`recentlyToasted`) keys on `{secret}::{terminalId}` → `message` so unchanged messages don't re-toast each long-poll tick, but changing messages (build stages) do. HS-7273 shipped Playwright coverage (`e2e/terminal-drawer-osc9.spec.ts` + `e2e/fixtures/terminal-osc9.sh` MODE-selectable fixture) with 4 tests — simple toast + bell-glyph + click-clears; dedupe; distinct messages; `9;4;3;50` progress parked — plus a 7-item manual-test-plan §12 checklist. Toast counts are captured via a MutationObserver pushing every `.hs-toast` add onto `window.__toastEvents` because the DOM only ever hosts one toast at a time. Follow-up **HS-7272 (native Tauri notification) shipped — see §30**.

**Status:** Shipped — server scanner + `/api/projects/bell-state` + `/api/terminal/list` + client toast dispatch, plus 8 unit tests in `registry.test.ts` and updated `projects.test.ts` for the new map shape.

---

## 30. OSC 9 native OS notifications (`30-osc9-native-notifications.md`)

HS-7272. Completes the OSC 9 story from §27 by adding a native OS notification that fires **alongside** the toast when Hot Sheet's window is backgrounded (`document.hidden || !document.hasFocus()`), so a user who isn't currently looking at Hot Sheet still sees the message in the Notification Center / system tray.

Tauri plumbing: `src-tauri/Cargo.toml` adds `tauri-plugin-notification = "2"`; `src-tauri/src/lib.rs` registers `.plugin(tauri_plugin_notification::init())` and exposes a `show_native_notification(title, body)` `#[tauri::command]` that calls `app.notification().builder().title(title).body(body).show()`; `src-tauri/capabilities/default.json` adds `"notification:default"`.

JS side (`src/client/tauriIntegration.tsx`): three exports — `requestNativeNotificationPermission()` (idempotent; reads `window.__TAURI__.notification`, calls `isPermissionGranted` then `requestPermission` if needed; called once from `app.tsx` boot), `fireNativeNotification(title, body)` (invokes `show_native_notification`, returns `false` in a browser context so the caller needs no Tauri guard), `isAppBackgrounded()` (the `document.hidden || !document.hasFocus()` gate).

Dispatch: `bellPoll.maybeFireNotificationToast` — the single choke-point for toast + native — now fires native alongside the toast when `isAppBackgrounded()` returns true, passing the active project's `name` as the notification title. Dedupe is shared with the toast via the pre-existing `recentlyToasted` Map: toast + native fire exactly once per unique `{secret}::{terminalId}` → message, and cache-entries GC when `/projects/bell-state` drops the notification so a subsequent identical-text message re-fires both channels.

11 unit tests in `tauriIntegration.test.ts` (new) cover permission idempotency, browser short-circuit, invoke success / rejection / fallback, and `isAppBackgrounded` across hidden / focused / both states — run in the default Node environment with manual `window` / `document` stubs (no jsdom dep added).

**Status:** Shipped — Rust plugin + command + capability, JS helpers + permission prime at boot, `bellPoll` dispatch gate, 11 unit tests. E2E for the backgrounded-app case is deferred (Playwright can't convincingly simulate the `window.__TAURI__.core` object and asserting OS banner rendering is beyond Chromium-only coverage — added to the manual test plan instead).

---

## 31. OSC 133 Phase 1b — Copy last output (`31-osc133-copy-last-output.md`)

HS-7268. Second user-visible affordance built on the Phase 1a (HS-7267) OSC 133 marker ring: a toolbar button that copies the most recent command's output to the clipboard. Range computation lives in a new pure helper `computeLastOutputRange(input)` in `src/client/terminalOsc133.ts` — takes `{ current, commands, cursorLine }`, returns `{ start, end } | null` with clear priority rules (in-flight record preferred when its C is alive, fall back to latest completed record, null when neither C is alive or the range is empty/inverted). The caller in `terminal.tsx`'s `copyLastOutput(inst)` walks the range via xterm's live buffer (`term.buffer.active.getLine(y).translateToString(true)`), trims trailing blanks, writes to `navigator.clipboard`, and flashes the Lucide `clipboard-copy` → `check` glyph green on success (`.copied` class, 900 ms revert) or shakes it on no-op (`.shake` keyframe, 350 ms).

Visibility is gated on `shellIntegration.enabled`: the button is rendered with `display:none` in the initial tab markup, revealed via `applyShellIntegrationToolbarVisibility` on first OSC 133 A, re-hidden by `resetShellIntegration` on PTY restart. Users whose shells don't emit OSC 133 see no toolbar change. 12 new unit tests in `terminalOsc133.test.ts` cover empty records / no-C / disposed-C / alive-C-and-D / alive-C-disposed-D / in-flight preferred over completed / in-flight with disposed-C fallback / in-flight without C / multiple completeds (latest-only) / empty range / inverted range / running on first line. E2E deferred to follow-up HS-7327 (Playwright spec + output-only fixture extension + `navigator.clipboard` assertion). Manual test plan §26 seven-item checklist shipped.

**Status:** Shipped + e2e (HS-7327). `computeLastOutputRange` helper + button + wiring + CSS + 12 unit tests. Playwright e2e in `e2e/terminal-osc133-copy-output.spec.ts` (2 tests: button stays hidden when no OSC 133 fires; complete A→B→C→output→D cycle reveals the button + click writes C→D range to navigator.clipboard) backed by `e2e/fixtures/terminal-osc133.sh` MODE=output / MODE=none. Critical fixture-config detail: lazy:true + skip POST /api/terminal/restart so the websocket attach itself triggers the spawn — restart would trigger the HS-6799 eager-spawn Ctrl-L redraw which the one-shot fixture has no way to handle.

---

## 32. OSC 133 Phase 2 — Jump shortcuts + hover popover (`32-osc133-jump-and-popover.md`)

HS-7269. Turns the Phase 1 marker ring into navigable + actionable UI: `Cmd/Ctrl+Up/Down` scrolls the xterm viewport to the prev/next `promptStart` marker via a new pure helper `findPromptLine(input)` in `terminalOsc133.ts` (9 new unit tests). The custom key handler is attached per-term via `term.attachCustomKeyEventHandler` and returns `false` to swallow the keystroke so no `\e[1;5A` leaks into the shell input even on the no-target case. Hover popover mounts on every gutter glyph with three buttons — Copy command (B→C via `readRecordCommand`), Copy output (C→D or C→cursor via `readRecordOutput`), Rerun (`term.paste(commandText + '\r')`). Single shared popover element positioned via `getBoundingClientRect` relative to the glyph; 200 ms close timer on mouseleave cancelled by popover `mouseenter` so users can leave glyph → popover without the popover vanishing.

New per-project setting `shell_integration_ui: boolean` (default true) added to `AppSettings`, persisted via `/api/settings` PATCH, surfaced as a checkbox under Settings → Terminal with hint. Toggling fires a `hotsheet:shell-integration-ui-changed` custom event that triggers `reapplyShellIntegrationDecorations` (dispose-or-re-register gutter decorations across every instance) + `applyShellIntegrationToolbarVisibility` (show/hide Phase 1b copy-output button). The OSC 133 parser still runs while the setting is off — markers keep accumulating so re-enabling restores the UI against the complete history. `attachGutterDecoration` and the keydown handler both check `shellIntegrationUiEnabled()` on every call so the setting flip takes effect immediately without a PTY restart.

**Status:** Shipped + e2e (HS-7328). Keyboard handler + `jumpToPromptMarker` + popover + helpers + setting plumbing + 9 unit tests. Playwright e2e in `e2e/terminal-osc133-jump-popover.spec.ts` (2 tests against MODE=multi: three OSC 133 cycles render 3 gutter glyphs / popover surfaces on hover with Copy command / Copy output / Rerun / Copy command writes to navigator.clipboard / Cmd or Ctrl + ArrowUp via platform-detected `navigator.userAgent.includes('Mac')` is intercepted as a jump rather than forwarded as `\e[1;5A`; Settings UI toggle: open Settings → Terminal tab → uncheck `#settings-shell-integration-ui` → glyph count drops to 0 — drives the actual checkbox because the `hotsheet:shell-integration-ui-changed` event is dispatched from the change handler, not from a settings poll).

---

## 33. OSC 133 Phase 3 — Ask Claude (`33-osc133-ask-claude.md`)

HS-7270. Final phase of the OSC 133 rollout and the Hot-Sheet-specific wedge vs. VS Code's terminal (see design doc §26.3 item 5): a fourth **Ask Claude** button in the Phase 2 popover, gated on `isChannelAlive()` at popover open time (absent entirely when the channel is down). The button is accent-colored + bold so it reads as the headline action on a red-X failed command. Click fires `askClaudeAboutRecord(inst, term, record)` which reads the record's B→C command text + C→D output via the Phase 2 helpers, packs them into a canonical diagnose-and-fix prompt via `buildAskClaudePrompt({command, exitCode, cwd, output, maxOutputChars})` — new pure helper in `terminalOsc133.ts` — and dispatches via `triggerChannelAndMarkBusy(message)` (existing channel entry point).

Template: ``The command `$CMD` exited with code $N in `$CWD`. Output:\n\n```\n$OUTPUT\n```\n\nPlease diagnose and propose a fix.`` with four variations: null cwd drops the "in `...`" clause, null exit code renders "(no exit code reported)", empty output renders `*(no output captured)*`, output over `maxOutputChars` (default 8 000 chars ~= 2 000 tokens) tail-truncates with a `[output truncated to last N chars]` header so Claude sees the failing tail rather than successful startup. 9 new unit tests cover every variation path.

Explicit non-goals (§33.5): `shell_analysis` command-log event type (follow-up HS-7332 if users ask), customizable prompt template, multi-command context, Ask-and-file-as-ticket workflow. The single diagnose-and-fix prompt covers the 90% case; deferring the rest keeps Phase 3 tight.

**Status:** Shipped + e2e (HS-7332). Helper + click action + popover wiring + CSS + 9 unit tests. Playwright e2e in `e2e/terminal-osc133-ask-claude.spec.ts` (2 tests against MODE=fail: channel alive via `page.route(/\/api\/channel\/status/) → {alive:true}` reveals Ask Claude button → click POSTs canonical prompt with command + exit code + output to /api/channel/trigger; channel dead with alive:false → button absent from popover). Route stubs use regex literals because the `?project=<secret>` query string breaks glob matching. All four OSC 133 phases (1a / 1b / 2 / 3) now shipped + e2e — HS-7265 spike fully closed. The optional shell_analysis command-log event type from §33.5 remains deferred (no user-facing value over the channel log already capturing the trigger).

---

## 34. Terminal find / search (`34-terminal-search.md`)

HS-7331. Every xterm surface in the app gets a collapsible find widget wrapping xterm's `SearchAddon`. Mount points: (a) the drawer terminal's toolbar — a new `.terminal-search-slot` placeholder between `.terminal-header-spacer` and the copy-output / power / clear buttons — and (b) **(HS-8341, 2026-05-13)** the dashboard dedicated view's top toolbar (`.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-bar`), right-aligned via `margin-left: auto` on the `.terminal-search-box` child rule. Pre-HS-8341 (b) mounted into a `#terminal-dashboard-search-slot` div in the app-header that was always occluded by the fixed-position overlay (`position: fixed; inset: 0; z-index: 600`), so the user never actually saw the widget. Grid tile xterms are deliberately excluded — preview-scale and non-interactive, per §34.1. The collapsed state is a 28 px magnifier button; clicking (or `Cmd/Ctrl+F` when the terminal is focused) adds `.is-open` and expands the box to 240 px with an input, prev / next chevrons, and a 1-based `N/M` result count. `Enter` finds next, `Shift+Enter` finds previous, `Esc` blurs the input (HS-7393) — the widget stays expanded with its query + highlights intact; the close (×) button is the explicit close/clear. Input `input` events run an incremental `findNext` so the active match moves as you type. Highlight palette uses amber / orange (not the accent blue) so matches stay distinct from the HS-7330 accent-tinted text selection. Widget logic lives in `src/client/terminalSearch.tsx` — `mountTerminalSearch(term, addon, opts?)` builds DOM + attaches handlers + returns a `TerminalSearchHandle`, `focusActiveTerminalSearch()` is the Cmd/Ctrl+F dispatch target (walks the last-active-handle tracker, verifies the root is still in the DOM, opens it — falls back to the ticket search on no-match), `_resetTerminalSearchForTests()` is the unit-test seam. The global Cmd/Ctrl+F handler in `shortcuts.tsx` calls `isTerminalFocused()` first (already exported for HS-6472) and when true routes to `focusActiveTerminalSearch()`; xterm's own `attachCustomKeyEventHandler` for both the drawer and dedicated-view xterms also returns `false` on Cmd/Ctrl+F so xterm doesn't forward `f` to the shell (returning false only stops xterm's internal processing — the DOM event still bubbles to `document` where the shortcut handler catches it).

**Non-goals (§34.6):** multi-terminal search (deferred), grid tile search (intentional — only full-screen mode per ticket spec). Regex / case / whole-word toggles (HS-7361 design) shipped as §34.8 under HS-7426. Recent-query history (HS-7362 design) shipped as §34.9 under HS-7427.

**Status:** Shipped v1 + e2e (HS-7363) + recent-query history (HS-7427) + match-mode toggles (HS-7426) + **HS-8341 (2026-05-13)** dedicated-view widget moved from the app-header slot directly into `.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-bar` via the new `attachDedicatedBarSearch(bar, term, label)` helper (exported from `src/client/terminalDashboard.tsx`, threaded through both `buildFlowDedicatedBarMount` + `buildSectionedDedicatedBarMount`). The `#terminal-dashboard-search-slot` div in `pages.tsx` + the `.terminal-dashboard-search-slot` CSS rule were deleted; the new CSS rule is `.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-bar > .terminal-search-box { margin-left: auto }`. HS-7526 capture-phase Esc handler updated to recover the widget root via `dashboardState.dedicatedSearchHandle.root` rather than the deleted slot id. Test coverage: 4 new DOM-level unit tests in `terminalDashboard.test.ts` (widget root appended to bar; placeholder threads entry label; addon loaded onto term exactly once; idempotent disposer removes the root); existing Playwright `dedicated view ... search slot` e2e test rewritten to use the dedicated-bar locator + new HS-8341 grid-view regression that asserts `.terminal-dashboard-dedicated-bar` count is 0 when no dedicated view is up. New deps: `@xterm/addon-search@0.16` (prod), `happy-dom` (dev — vitest DOM environment for the new tests). New files: `src/client/terminalSearch.tsx` + `src/client/terminalSearch.test.ts` (14 unit tests covering mount / focus / close / toggle / Enter / Shift+Enter / incremental / empty-input-clears / Esc / count chip updates / zero-results / dispose / active-handle routing), `docs/34-terminal-search.md`. Config: `vitest.config.ts` gained `resolve.alias` for `#jsx/jsx-runtime` + `#jsx/jsx-dev-runtime` so .tsx files are importable from tests; `src/jsx-runtime.ts` now exports `jsxDEV` as an alias for `jsx` so the dev-mode JSX transform can resolve it. CSS `.terminal-search-box` (+ `.is-open` expansion + `.terminal-search-toggle` / `-input` / `-count` / `-btn` children) and `.terminal-dashboard-search-slot` in `styles.scss`. Pages markup (`pages.tsx`) adds the dashboard slot next to the sizer. Wiring: `terminal.tsx` mountXterm loads SearchAddon + mounts the widget + stores on `TerminalInstance.search` / `.searchHandle`, teardown disposes the handle before the xterm; `terminalDashboard.tsx` openDedicatedView + exitDedicatedView + teardownAllTiles do the symmetric thing for the dedicated view's xterm. Plus HS-7363 Playwright e2e — 4 tests in `e2e/terminal-search.spec.ts` backed by `e2e/fixtures/terminal-search-fruits.sh` (prints `apple\nbanana\napple\napple\n` then `exec sleep 3600`): drawer flow (open + count walks `1/3 → 2/3 → 3/3 → 2/3` across Enter / Shift+Enter + HS-7393 Esc-blur-keeps-query assertion + × close clears+collapses), Cmd+F routing (focus xterm helper → Meta+f → assert terminal-search input focused + `#search-input` not focused), dashboard dedicated-view (enter dashboard with sizer visible / slot hidden → dblclick tile → slot visible / sizer hidden → run the same `1/3` search → Back → sizer restored / slot hidden), grid-view regression (slot stays hidden in grid). `docs/34-terminal-search.md` §34.7 rewritten to describe shipped e2e + narrower manual scope; `docs/manual-test-plan.md` §13 trimmed to the remaining visual-color / fallback-path / state-reset checks with an "e2e-covered" preamble + Automated Coverage Summary gets a new bullet. tsc + lint clean, 1110/1110 unit tests pass (+14 over baseline). Cross-refs: §22 (drawer terminal toolbar), §25 §25.4 (dashboard tile-size slider / slot sharing), §32 (OSC 133 jump-to-prompt — orthogonal structured nav).

## 35. Terminal theme + font (`35-terminal-themes.md`)

HS-6307. Every xterm surface in Hot Sheet (drawer, dashboard tile, dashboard dedicated view) renders with a configurable **appearance** — color palette + font family + font size — resolved per-terminal from a three-layer stack: session override (dynamic terminals only, in-memory `Map<terminalId, Partial<TerminalAppearance>>`) > configured override (per-terminal `theme` / `fontFamily` / `fontSize` fields on `TerminalConfig` in `settings.json`) > project default (`terminal_default: { theme, fontFamily, fontSize }` in `settings.json`) > hard-coded fallback (`{ theme: 'default', fontFamily: 'system', fontSize: 13 }`). Each field resolves independently so a configured terminal with `{ theme: 'dracula' }` but no font override still inherits the project-default font.

11 curated themes (`default` — CSS-var-derived preserving HS-7330 behavior — plus Dracula, Solarized Dark / Light, Nord, Gruvbox Dark, Monokai, One Dark, Tomorrow Night, GitHub Dark / Light). 11 fonts (`system` — the existing OS mono stack — plus 10 Google Fonts monospaced faces: JetBrains Mono, Fira Code, Source Code Pro, IBM Plex Mono, Roboto Mono, Inconsolata, Ubuntu Mono, Space Mono, Anonymous Pro, Cascadia Code). Font size clamped to `[8, 32]`. Adding a new theme or font later is a single-entry append to the ordered arrays in `src/client/terminalThemes.ts` / `terminalFonts.ts` — the Settings UI + gear popover re-render their `<select>` options from those arrays on every open, so no code changes elsewhere.

Per-terminal gear button (Lucide `settings`) sits to the right of clear on the terminal toolbar. Click opens a small floating popover anchored below the button with a theme select, font select, font-size numeric input with −/+ steppers, and a "Reset to project default" link. Changes apply instantly to the live xterm via `term.options.theme = …`, `.fontFamily = …`, `.fontSize = …`. For configured terminals, popover changes persist through `/file-settings` PATCH; for dynamic terminals, changes stay in the session-override map (cleared on page reload, survives PTY restart so user tweaks aren't lost on Stop/Start). Popover dismissal: click outside, press Escape, or click the gear again. Only one popover open at a time.

Project-default panel lives at the top of Settings → Terminal with the same three controls (theme / font / font-size). Writes through to `terminal_default` in `settings.json` via `/file-settings` PATCH, dispatches the `hotsheet:terminal-default-changed` custom event, and every mounted xterm re-resolves + re-applies its appearance. Per-terminal overrides stay in place — only fields that were inheriting from the default pick up the new value.

Google Fonts loaded at runtime via a dynamic `<link rel="stylesheet">` tag appended to `<head>` (idempotent per font id — same `data-terminal-font-id` attribute + Map-cached promise so concurrent calls share one network request); `document.fonts.load('13px "<family>"')` awaited before xterm re-renders so the canvas doesn't flash System glyphs for a frame. Offline failure mode: `document.fonts.load` resolves empty, xterm falls back through the CSS font-family cascade to the System stack — no error popup, no retry loop.

**Cross-surface consistency.** The dashboard tile's xterm mount reads `TerminalListEntry` (now carrying the `theme` / `fontFamily` / `fontSize` fields from `/terminal/list`) + the cached project default + the session-override map via a shared `resolveTileAppearance(tile)` helper. The dashboard dedicated view does the same. Every surface applies the font asynchronously post-`term.open` via `applyAppearanceToTerm(term, appearance)`; the theme is applied synchronously at `new XTerm({ theme: … })` via `themeToXtermOptions(getThemeById(appearance.theme))` so the first paint is correct. Both dashboard and drawer subscribe to `hotsheet:terminal-default-changed` so project-default edits propagate across every live terminal without a page reload.

**Out of scope (v1):** custom user themes (code-owned registry), transparent / wallpaper backgrounds, ligatures toggle, non-Google-Fonts families, bold / italic weight overrides, dashboard tile gear popover (tiles are preview-only — change appearance from the drawer or dedicated view), keyboard shortcut to open the popover.

**Status:** Shipped. New files: `src/client/terminalThemes.ts` + `.test.ts` (13 tests), `src/client/terminalFonts.ts` + `.test.ts` (16 tests), `src/client/terminalAppearance.ts` + `.test.ts` (20 tests), `src/client/terminalAppearancePopover.tsx` (gear popover UI), `src/client/terminalDefaultAppearanceUI.tsx` (Settings → Terminal panel). Wired into `src/client/terminal.tsx` mountXterm + `reapplyAppearance` + `hotsheet:terminal-default-changed` subscription; `src/client/terminalDashboard.tsx` `mountTileXterm` + `enterDedicatedView` both route through `resolveTileAppearance`. Pages markup (`src/routes/pages.tsx`) gains the "Default appearance" panel markup at the top of the Terminal settings tab + a gear button in every terminal toolbar via the existing `.terminal-header-btn` class. `TerminalConfig` (`src/terminals/config.ts`) gains optional `theme` / `fontFamily` / `fontSize` fields; `normalizeConfig` type-checks each. `file-settings.ts`'s loose Zod schema passes `terminal_default` through unchanged. Docs: new `docs/35-terminal-themes.md` (spec), this §35 entry, dashboard row below. Follow-ups filed: custom user themes, dashboard tile gear popover.

Cross-refs: §22 (base terminal toolbar hosts the gear button), §25 (dashboard tile + dedicated view share the appearance resolution), HS-7330 (the CSS-var-derived theme this feature generalises; the `default` theme preserves that behavior exactly).

## 36. Drawer terminal grid view (`36-drawer-terminal-grid.md`)

HS-6311. Per-project tile grid inside the drawer — conceptually a project-scoped version of the global Terminal Dashboard (§25). Toggle button `#drawer-grid-toggle` sits in the drawer toolbar's `.drawer-tabs-end` cluster (before the expand button) using the Lucide `layout-grid` glyph; slider `#drawer-grid-sizer` sits just before the toggle and is shown only while grid mode is active. Both render on web + Tauri (HS-8624 removed the §22.11 / §25.2 Tauri-only gate). The toggle is **disabled** (not hidden) when the project has ≤1 terminal, enables as soon as a second terminal exists, and auto-exits grid mode if the count drops back below 2 while grid is active.

Grid mode swaps the drawer body from the per-terminal tab stack to a flex-wrap grid of 4:3 tiles covering every terminal in the CURRENT project. Tile math reuses `terminalDashboardSizing.ts` verbatim (`tileWidthFromColumnCount`, `perRowToSliderPosition`, `sliderPositionToPerRow`, `computeTileScale`, `tileNativeGridFromCellMetrics`, `computeColumnSnapPoints`, `legacySliderValueToColumnCount`, same snap-tick rendering as §25 — post-HS-8242 the slider semantics are inverted to a column-count integer in `[1, 10]`, default `4`). Tiles are non-interactive except for click/dblclick/context-menu; single-click → FLIP-animated centered overlay at 90 % of the drawer body (vs §25.7's 70 % — drawer is already short); double-click → `.drawer-terminal-grid-dedicated` inner overlay running `FitAddon.fit()` on a fresh xterm + `applyDedicatedHistoryFrame` post-replay refit (HS-7063 pattern). Back / Esc returns to the grid or centered state, clicking a drawer terminal tab or the Commands Log button auto-exits grid mode and activates that tab (mirrors §25.3 rule 3).

Lazy / exited tiles render as placeholder boxes with a muted play glyph + status string (`Not yet started` / `Exited (code N)`); click spawns + transitions to centered, dblclick spawns + goes straight to dedicated. Bells ring the same bounce keyframe + persistent 2 px accent outline via `subscribeToBellState`; `POST /api/terminal/clear-bell` fires on center / dedicated enter. PTY follow-back on dedicated exit (`exitDedicatedView` re-sends the tile's target cols × rows) matches §25's HS-7097 follow-up so the tile doesn't display bytes formatted for the dedicated pane geometry after the dedicated view closes.

State is per-project + session-only via two new `Map<secret, …>` structures in `state.tsx` (`projectGridActive` + `projectGridColumnCount`, default `false` / `4` — post-HS-8242 the value is the user-facing column count integer; `legacySliderValueToColumnCount` migrates pre-HS-8242 persisted floats on read), with `clearPerProjectSessionState(secret)` wiping both. The corresponding file-settings key is `dashboard_columns_per_row` (renamed from `dashboard_slider_value`). Grid-mode flag survives a project switch but resets on page reload (no `file-settings` persistence in v1). No server-side changes — every attach / clear-bell flow already exists.

**Status:** Shipped. New files: `src/client/drawerTerminalGrid.tsx` (the grid shell + tile lifecycle + centered overlay + dedicated view), `docs/36-drawer-terminal-grid.md` (spec), `e2e/drawer-terminal-grid.spec.ts` (3 tests: toggle disabled with ≤1 terminal + enabled + on/off + tile count; slider persists per project across exit+re-enter; tab-click exits grid + activates that tab). Extended: `src/client/state.tsx` (+8 unit tests in `state.test.ts` for default/setter/round-trip/clear/no-leak), `src/routes/pages.tsx` (toggle + slider markup + grid container), `src/client/styles.scss` (grid + tile + centered overlay + dedicated view + bell bounce), `src/client/terminal.tsx` (list-update hook + auto-exit-on-activate), `src/client/commandLog.tsx` (auto-exit on `switchDrawerTab`), `src/client/app.tsx` (`initDrawerTerminalGrid` + `onExitGrid` wiring). Follow-ups: CWD badge on drawer-grid tiles (the dashboard has one per HS-7278), keyboard shortcut to toggle grid mode, extraction of shared tile-grid module from §25 + §36.

Cross-refs: §22 (base drawer terminal feature), §25 (global dashboard this feature mirrors at per-project scope), §23 (bell Phase 1), §24 (cross-project bell long-poll that drives the tile indicator), §4.1 (top toolbar is deliberately untouched — the grid lives in the drawer toolbar only).

## 37. Quit confirmation when terminals are running (`37-quit-confirm.md`)

HS-7591 (req-change spec) + HS-7596 (implementation). macOS Terminal.app-style "Ask before closing" gating across every quit path so users don't silently lose running work. Three modes per project (`confirm_quit_with_running_terminals: 'always' | 'never' | 'with-non-exempt-processes'`, default `'with-non-exempt-processes'`) + a user-editable exempt list (`quit_confirm_exempt_processes`, default `{screen, tmux, less, more, view, mandoc, tail, log, top, htop}`). One-level-deeper rule for shell-rooted PTYs: when the configured `command` IS a shell (`bash`, `zsh`, `fish`, `sh`, `dash`, `ash`, `ksh`, `tcsh`, `pwsh`, `powershell`, `cmd`, `cmd.exe`), look at the foreground child of the shell to decide whether to prompt; the shell itself is treated as exempt (idle login shell). When the configured command is NOT a shell (e.g. `claude`, `npm run dev`), the root process is what's evaluated.

**Detection** (server-side, Unix only for v1 — Windows safe-defaults to "prompt"). `inspectForegroundProcess(rootPid, exemptList)` runs `ps -o pid,ppid,comm -A` once, parses to a parent→children map, walks the deepest descendant chain (highest-pid child at each level), then `pickForegroundProcess` applies the §37.3 one-level-deeper rule + exempt-list lookup (case-insensitive basename match). On any lookup failure (process exited mid-check, ps unavailable) returns the safe-default-prompt info — users prefer one extra confirmation over a silent kill. Pure helpers in `src/terminals/processInspect.ts` (parsePsOutput / descendantChain / pickForegroundProcess) covered by 22 unit tests.

**Routes.** `GET /api/terminal/foreground-process?terminalId=` returns the per-terminal info. `GET /api/projects/quit-summary` aggregates across every registered project: walks every alive PTY, inspects its foreground process, returns `{projects: [{secret, name, confirmMode, entries: [{terminalId, label, foregroundCommand, isShell, isExempt}]}]}`. The route does NOT decide whether to prompt — the client owns that policy because the prompt context (Tauri close vs. CLI --close vs. stale-instance cleanup) varies.

**Decision** (client-side, pure). `evaluateQuitDecision(summary)` in `src/client/quitConfirm.tsx` applies §37.5 across all projects: prompt fires if any project is `'always'` OR if any project's `'with-non-exempt-processes'` resolves to "has at least one non-exempt entry"; `'never'` projects don't trigger but contribute their alive entries to the displayed list (so users see what they're killing across every project). 9 unit tests in `quitConfirm.test.ts`.

**Tauri quit-handler.** `tauri::WindowEvent::CloseRequested` in `src-tauri/src/lib.rs` checks a `QuitConfirmed: AtomicBool` state. First close attempt: `api.prevent_close()` + emit `quit-confirm-requested` event. The JS frontend (`initQuitConfirm` listener via `__TAURI__.event.listen`) runs the confirm flow + on "Quit Anyway" invokes the new `confirm_quit` Tauri command. `confirm_quit` sets the AtomicBool to true and re-issues `window.close()`; the second CloseRequested fire sees the flag and lets the close proceed. `RunEvent::Exit` then kills the sidecar via the existing SIGTERM path.

**CLI `--close`.** Extends `handleClose` in `src/cli.ts` with a `confirmCloseAgainstQuitSummary` step before the DELETE: fetches /api/projects/quit-summary, filters to the project being closed, applies the §37.5 logic, prompts via stdin (`y/N`). New `--force` flag skips the prompt for non-interactive use.

**Settings UI.** Settings → Terminal gains a "Quit confirmation" section (`src/client/quitConfirmSettingsUI.tsx`) with the three radio modes + a textarea for the exempt list (one basename per line) + a "Reset exempt list to defaults" link. Saves are debounced + write through PATCH /api/file-settings. The exempt list is stored as JSON array (added to `JSON_VALUE_KEYS` in file-settings.ts).

**Don't ask again.** The dialog has a "Don't ask again for any project" checkbox that, on Quit Anyway, flips every project's `confirm_quit_with_running_terminals` to `'never'`. Power-user opt-out without leaving the dialog.

**Out of scope (v1):** per-terminal kill confirm (handled by existing tab-close/Stop flows), session save+restore on relaunch, graceful SIGINT/SIGTERM-then-SIGHUP escalation in the dialog (existing teardown signal flow handles it), cross-window aggregation across separate Tauri processes. Stale-instance cleanup intentionally bypasses since that path is programmatic + the user is already quitting through a new window.

**HS-7789 follow-up.** Quit-confirm dialog showed the raw `dyn-…` id for dynamic terminals. Root cause: `/api/projects/quit-summary` resolved labels via `listTerminalConfigs(dataDir)` only — that returns persisted (settings-backed) terminals, and dynamic terminals created via `POST /api/terminal/create` keep their friendly name in the in-memory `dynamicConfigs` map in `src/routes/terminal.ts`. New `listDynamicTerminalConfigs(secret)` export merges those into the label lookup. 2 regression tests in `projects.test.ts`.

**HS-7790 follow-up.** Quit prompt fired for an idle login zsh even with the with-non-exempt-processes mode + zsh in the exempt list. Root cause: macOS `ps -o comm` emits the executable's full path (e.g. `/bin/zsh`), and login shells additionally get a leading dash (`-zsh`). `parsePsOutput` previously stored those values verbatim and the downstream `SHELL_BASENAMES` + exempt-list comparisons silently failed. New `normalizeComm()` helper in `src/terminals/processInspect.ts` strips directory prefix, leading dash, and `.exe` suffix; applied in `parsePsOutput` so every downstream consumer sees a stable basename. 10 new tests cover the path / dash / .exe / idempotence / empty cases plus an end-to-end pickForegroundProcess assertion that an idle `/bin/zsh` resolves to "exempt shell" with `zsh` in the user's exempt list.

**HS-8604 (2026-05-25) — extended to project-tab close (§37.10).** Closing a project tab previously DELETEd immediately: it (a) **orphaned the project's PTYs** — `DELETE /api/projects/:secret` only cleared the project maps, leaving every terminal's process running unreachable until app exit, and `destroyProjectTerminals` was both uncalled AND latently broken (deleted `sessions` entries without `teardownPty`); (b) showed **no confirmation**, silently killing the very processes §37 guards. Fix: the DELETE route now calls (the now-correctly-tearing-down) `destroyProjectTerminals(secret)` before `unregisterProject`; the client's `removeProject` / `removeOtherProjects` / `removeProjectsInDirection` gate on a new `confirmCloseProjects(secrets)` (`quitConfirm.tsx`) that reuses the same per-project setting + `evaluateQuitDecision` scoped to the closing tab(s) and shows the lightweight `confirmDialog` (idle tabs never prompt; fetch failure proceeds since the server now kills PTYs cleanly). Tests: registry kill-PTYs-on-destroy, `projects.test.ts` DELETE-invokes-destroy, `buildCloseConfirmMessage`, new `quitConfirmCloseProjects.test.ts` decision matrix.

**Status:** Shipped (HS-7596; project-tab close added HS-8604). Cross-refs: §22 (base PTY lifecycle — quit-confirm gates IN FRONT OF destroyAllTerminals's existing SIGHUP path), §10 (Tauri shell hosts CloseRequested), §8 (CLI flags).

---

## 38. Persisted terminal visibility (`38-terminal-visibility.md`)

HS-7825. Configured-terminal hidden state (originally session-only, HS-7661) now survives reload + relaunch via the per-project `hidden_terminals` file-settings key (added to `JSON_VALUE_KEYS`). Dynamic terminals (`dyn-*`) intentionally remain session-only — their lifetime ends with the PTY, so persisting their hidden state would mean stale ids accumulating in settings.json forever. The filter happens at both read (`hydratePersistedHiddenForProject` skips them) and write (`computePersistedIds(allHidden)` strips them) paths. Implementation: new module `src/client/persistedHiddenTerminals.ts` owns the per-project debounced (250 ms) PATCH on every `subscribeToHiddenChanges` fire + the boot-time hydration; `initPersistedHiddenTerminals(projects)` is called from both `initProjectTabs` and `refreshProjectTabs` in `src/client/projectTabs.tsx`. New helpers in `src/client/dashboardHiddenTerminals.ts`: `isConfiguredTerminalId(id)` (returns `!id.startsWith('dyn-')`) and `hydratePersistedHiddenForProject(secret, ids)` (structurally compares so a same-content hydrate doesn't fire spurious notify). Tests: 4 unit tests for `hydratePersistedHiddenForProject` + 4 for `isConfiguredTerminalId` + 4 for `computePersistedIds`.

**HS-7829 follow-up — stale-id cleanup on terminal deletion.** New pure helper `prunedHiddenTerminals(currentHidden, configuredIds)` in `src/file-settings.ts` returns a filtered array (or `null` for no-op) when one or more hidden ids no longer exist in `terminals[]`. The `/file-settings` PATCH handler in `src/routes/settings.ts` calls it whenever the patch contains a `terminals` key (alongside the existing `eagerSpawnTerminals` step) and writes the pruned list when needed. 8 unit tests in `file-settings.test.ts`. See §38.7.

**HS-7830 follow-up — Reset visibility from Settings.** New "Reset visibility" button + status hint in Settings → Terminal (below the Default terminals list) clears the project's persisted hidden state without opening the Show / Hide Terminals dialog. Status hint shows the live hidden-count (or "No terminals hidden" when zero); button is disabled at zero. Click confirms via `confirmDialog` then calls `unhideAllInProject(secret)` — the existing persistence-layer subscription PATCHes `hidden_terminals: []` automatically. New module `src/client/hiddenTerminalsResetUI.tsx` (`loadAndWireHiddenTerminalsReset`), wired from `settingsDialog.tsx`'s on-open handler. See §38.8.

**Status:** Shipped (HS-7825 + HS-7829 + HS-7830). Generalised by §39 (HS-7826) — see below. Cross-refs: §25 (dashboard's Show / Hide Terminals dialog — global mode), §36 (drawer-grid Show / Hide Terminals dialog — single-project mode), §22.10 (`terminals[]` config the persistence layer keys against).

---

## 39. Visibility groupings (`39-visibility-groupings.md`)

HS-7826 / HS-8290 / HS-8406. Generalises §38's flat `hidden_terminals` shape into named **visibility groupings** so the user can switch between contexts (e.g. "claude only", "server logs", "single app") without re-toggling rows. **HS-8290 reshape** — pre-HS-8290 each project had its own grouping list with cross-project fan-out machinery to keep them aligned; post-HS-8290 the grouping list is global. Each grouping carries `{ id, name, hiddenByProject: Record<secret, string[]> }`; the system carries an ordered list of groupings + a per-scope active-grouping pick. A Default grouping (literal id `'default'`) is always present and refused for deletion (rename works since the id is the invariant).

**HS-8406 reshape — per-scope active selection.** HS-8290 collapsed the active-grouping selection into a single global `activeId`, which meant flipping the dropdown in a project's drawer-grid ALSO flipped the dashboard's pick (and every other project's). HS-8406 keeps the grouping LIST global but re-introduces per-scope active-grouping selection: each surface that reads/writes the active grouping uses its own scope key. The dashboard uses `'dashboard'`; each project's drawer-grid + the drawer-grid's hide-terminal dialog uses `'project:<secret>'`. The grouping definitions stay shared (one global list); only the "which grouping is currently active" pick is scoped. State shape: `GlobalVisibilityState = { groupings, activeIdByScope: Record<string, string> }`. Scopes missing from the map fall back to `DEFAULT_GROUPING_ID`; setting a scope back to Default strips its entry to keep the persisted payload byte-stable.

**Persistence (HS-8290 → HS-8406).** Single source of truth in `~/.hotsheet/config.json` under `dashboard.visibilityGroupings` + `dashboard.activeVisibilityGroupingIdByScope` (HS-8406 — the per-scope map). The legacy scalar `dashboard.activeVisibilityGroupingId` keeps being written for one release as the dashboard scope's mirror so a downgrade-then-upgrade flow doesn't lose the dashboard's pick; `parsePersistedState` accepts both shapes and migrates the legacy scalar into `{ dashboard: <id> }` when the new map is absent. Six per-project keys (`visibility_groupings`, `active_visibility_grouping_id`, `hidden_terminals`, `dashboard_layout_mode`, `dashboard_columns_per_row`, `dashboard_slider_value`) are reserved as dead keys in `src/file-settings.ts::HS_8290_DEAD_KEYS` — `readFileSettings` strips them on read so old settings.json files stop surfacing stale values. No migration step for the HS-8290 reshape (per the HS-8290 ticket the feature wasn't public so existing values are dropped); the HS-8406 reshape carries the legacy scalar for compat.

**UI changes.** The Show / Hide Terminals dialog has a tab bar at the top: Default tab leftmost (always present), `+` button at end (Lucide `plus`, opens an in-app name prompt), right-click context menu (Rename… / Delete with Default's Delete disabled), HTML5 drag-and-drop to reorder, horizontally scrollable strip for many groupings. Toggling a row writes against the dialog's scope's active grouping's `hiddenByProject[group.secret]`. Paired footer buttons: **Show All** (`unhideAllEverywhereInGrouping(activeId)` — clears every project in the dialog's scope's active grouping) and **Hide All** (`hideAllInGrouping(secret, activeId, ids)` per project). A `<select>` dropdown next to the eye icon (dashboard + drawer-grid) appears when `groupings.length > 1` and lets the user switch the surface's active grouping without opening the dialog. The dashboard's dropdown affects only the dashboard scope; each project's drawer-grid dropdown affects only that project's scope.

**Implementation (HS-8290 → HS-8406).** Pure helpers in `src/client/visibilityGroupings.ts` operating on `GlobalVisibilityState` (`addGrouping`, `renameGrouping`, `deleteGrouping`, `reorderGroupings`, `setActiveGroupingIdFor(state, scopeKey, id)`, `getActiveGroupingFor(state, scopeKey)`, `getActiveGroupingIdFor(state, scopeKey)`, `toggleHiddenInGrouping`, `parsePersistedState(rawGroupings, rawLegacyId, rawActiveIdByScope?)`, `pruneStaleIdsInGroupings`). Two scope-key helpers exported: `DASHBOARD_SCOPE` and `projectScope(secret)`. `deleteGrouping` strips per-scope overrides that pointed at the deleted grouping (those scopes fall back to Default on next read). State in `src/client/dashboardHiddenTerminals.tsx` is a single global slot. Every public read/write helper takes a `scopeKey` first arg: `isTerminalHidden(scopeKey, secret, terminalId)`, `setTerminalHidden(scopeKey, secret, terminalId, hide)`, `filterVisible(scopeKey, secret, entries)`, `getHiddenTerminals(scopeKey, secret)`, `unhideAllInProject(scopeKey, secret)`, `unhideAllEverywhere(scopeKey)`, `countHiddenAcrossAllProjects(scopeKey)`, `countHiddenForProject(scopeKey, secret)`, `getActiveGroupingId(scopeKey)`, `setActiveGrouping(scopeKey, id)`. Persistence in `persistedHiddenTerminals.ts` does a single global debounced PATCH to `/api/global-config` writing the new map + the legacy scalar. `visibilityGroupingSelect.tsx`'s `GroupingSelectOptions` carries a lazy `getScopeKey: () => string` resolver — the dashboard returns `() => DASHBOARD_SCOPE`, the drawer-grid returns `() => projectScope(getActiveProject()?.secret ?? '')` so a project switch picks up the new secret without a re-wire. The dashboard tile context-menu's "Hide in Dashboard" writes against `DASHBOARD_SCOPE`; the drawer-grid tile context-menu's "Hide in Dashboard" writes against `projectScope(secret)`.

**Out of scope.** Duplicate-grouping affordance, keyboard shortcuts (Cmd/Ctrl+1..9), live cross-window sync of active grouping.

**Status:** Shipped (HS-7826 + HS-8290 + HS-8406). Tests: `visibilityGroupings.test.ts` (47 tests including HS-8406 per-scope selection + migration coverage), `dashboardHiddenTerminals.test.ts` (29 tests, every helper exercised through the dashboard scope plus a per-scope independence test), `persistedHiddenTerminals.test.ts` + `visibilityGroupingsStore.test.ts` + `showHideTerminalsIntegration.test.ts` updated to thread `DASHBOARD_SCOPE`. Cross-refs: §38 (single-grouping precursor), §25 (dashboard dialog opener), §36 (drawer-grid dialog opener), §22.10 (terminals[] config).
