## 51. Per-terminal shell history scoping (`51-shell-history.md`)

HS-7964 (investigation) / HS-7965 (implementation). Each Hot Sheet terminal gets its own up-arrow history pool, scoped per (project, terminal id), so commands typed in project A's `zsh` terminal don't bleed into project B's `zsh` terminal — and the Claude tab's nothing isn't mixed with the shell tab's recall.

**Why the simple `HISTFILE` env-var fix isn't enough.** Verified empirically: setting `HISTFILE` in the PTY's spawn env is silently clobbered on default-macOS zsh because `/etc/zshrc_Apple_Terminal` rewrites `HISTFILE` to a per-session file, and that rc runs AFTER our env injection but BEFORE the user's interactive prompt. So the fix has to inject AFTER the user's rc loads, which means using each shell's init-file override hook.

**Per-shell mechanism.** bash uses `--rcfile <path>` CLI rewrite (env vars don't work — bash interactive shells only honour `--rcfile` for non-login interactive). zsh uses `ZDOTDIR=<dir>` env (cleanest). fish uses `XDG_CONFIG_HOME=<dir>` env + indexes by session NAME via `set -x fish_history hotsheet_<projectHash>_<terminalId>`. Other shells (sh / dash / ksh / pwsh / cmd) skipped — no equivalent override worth implementing.

**Storage.** `<dataDir>/.hotsheet/shell_init/<terminalId>/` for generated rc files, `<dataDir>/.hotsheet/shell_history/<terminalId>` for bash + zsh history files. Fish history lands wherever fish puts it under the redirected `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` (session-name keyed by 8-char SHA-256-hex of dataDir + terminalId so multi-project doesn't collide). All under `<dataDir>/.hotsheet/` which is gitignored.

**Wire-up.** New `src/terminals/shellHistory.ts` exposes `setupShellHistoryForSpawn({dataDir, terminalId, command}): {env, rewrittenCommand, shell}` + 9 pure helpers. `src/terminals/registry.ts::spawnIntoSession` calls it after `resolveTerminalCommand`; the PTY spawn uses `command: rewrittenCommand ?? resolved.command` (bash gets `--rcfile` injection; others unchanged) and `env: buildEnv(shellInit.env)` (existing scrub + standard vars + per-shell override vars). `buildEnv` extended from no-arg → `buildEnv(extra: Record<string, string> = {})`.

**Settings.** New per-project key `terminal_history_scope: 'per-terminal' | 'inherit'` (default `'per-terminal'`). `'inherit'` falls back to pre-fix behavior (no override). No UI in v1 — power users edit settings.json by hand.

**Status:** Shipped. 25 unit tests in `shellHistory.test.ts` covering classification (path / args / .exe / case / unrecognised / empty), scope normalisation, shell-escape, fish-name sanitisation, all 4 init-file builders, and bash command rewrite (bare / with-args / already-has-rcfile / login-shell-skip / quote-escaping).

**Out of scope.** Windows PowerShell + cmd history scoping (separate ticket if asked); migration of the user's existing global history; cross-terminal recall (`atuin` does this externally); TUI-level history (Claude / vim / less own their own state); GC sweep of orphaned per-terminal init dirs (low priority — files are tiny).

**Cross-refs:** §22 (base terminal — where the spawn lives), §2 (settings.json schema home for the new key), HS-7964 (parent investigation).

## 53. Streaming shell-command output (`53-streaming-shell-output.md`)

**Status:** Shipped — Phase 1 + 2 + 3 + 4 (HS-7982 + HS-7983 + HS-7984). HS-7981 design spike picked Option A — periodic polling of partial output — over SSE / WebSocket / dedicated-stream alternatives because it composes with the existing `commandSidebar.tsx::startShellPoll` 2 s `setInterval` loop, requires zero new connections, and the 4 MB per-command cap keeps the simple full-buffer approach affordable. Closes the "60 s of nothing then everything lands at once" UX gap for custom shell commands run via `POST /api/shell/exec`.

**Phase 1 server-side buffer (HS-7982).** `src/routes/shell.ts` adds `partialOutputs = new Map<number, string>()` keyed on log id, fed by both `child.stdout.on('data')` and `child.stderr.on('data')` via `recordPartialChunk(logId, chunk)` so the buffer interleaves both streams in event order. Pure helper `appendPartialOutput(prev, chunk)` enforces the 4 MB cap by dropping the HEAD bytes and prepending `[output truncated]\n` when the post-append length exceeds `PARTIAL_OUTPUT_CAP` — the most recent bytes are always preserved so a polling client sees the freshest output even from a chatty `yes`-style command. Entry deleted on `child.on('close')` AND `child.on('error')` so failed-to-spawn commands don't leak.

**Phase 2 endpoint extension (HS-7982).** `GET /api/shell/running` response shape upgraded from `{ ids: number[] }` to `{ ids: number[]; outputs: Record<number, string> }`. The `outputs` map is always present (`{}` when no processes are running) so consumers don't need optional-chaining. Backwards compatible — clients ignoring the new field continue to work as before. The delta-protocol alternative (`/shell/output?ids=...&offsets=...`) was rejected as v1 over-spec; the 4 MB cap keeps payloads bounded. Verified via `commandSidebar.tsx::startShellPoll` continuing to ignore `outputs` until HS-7983 lands.

**Tests.** 5 server-side unit tests in `src/routes/shell.test.ts` (HS-7982): empty `outputs` map default, partial-output visible mid-run, buffer dropped on close. 3 unit tests on the pure helper covering append below cap / append exceeding cap (head-truncation + marker + most-recent-bytes preserved) / single chunk that itself exceeds the cap. 32 client-side tests (HS-7983): 12 in `stripAnsi.test.ts` for the new client-local pure helpers, 8 in `commandSidebar.test.ts` for `decideShellPartialEvents` (dedup-by-length / drop-finished-id / preserve-pre-first-chunk / older-server-no-outputs / multi-id concurrent), 12 in `commandLog.test.ts` for `shouldAutoScrollToBottom` (sticky-bottom thresholds + sub-pixel rounding + custom threshold) AND a happy-dom integration suite for `applyShellPartialEvent` (text-strip / overwrite-on-subsequent-chunks / no-container no-op / no-matching-id no-op / multi-entry isolation).

**Phase 3 client modules (HS-7983).** New `src/client/stripAnsi.ts` exports `stripAnsi` + `tailLines` (mirror of `src/terminals/scrollbackSnapshot.ts`'s pure helpers — kept client-local so esbuild doesn't pull in the server-side `Buffer`-using `buildScrollbackPreview`). `commandSidebar.tsx` exports `decideShellPartialEvents` + `SHELL_PARTIAL_OUTPUT_EVENT` + `ShellPartialOutputEvent` and `runShellCommand` now takes an optional `btnEl` so `attachShellPreviewToButton(btn, id)` can mount a `<div class="channel-command-preview">` after the originating button + listen for `hotsheet:shell-partial-output` + render `tailLines(stripAnsi(partial), 2)`. `startShellPoll(id, onComplete?)` invokes the cleanup callback the moment the run finishes so the preview tears down with the global busy indicator. `commandLog.tsx` exports `shouldAutoScrollToBottom` + `applyShellPartialEvent`; `renderLogEntry` adds a third branch for running shell entries (no `---SHELL_OUTPUT---` separator yet) that renders a dedicated `<pre class="command-log-shell-partial" data-shell-partial-id={id}>` targeted by the listener. Sticky-bottom auto-scroll captures pinned-state BEFORE the textContent swap (the swap grows scrollHeight, which would otherwise always make the post-write distance look bigger). SCSS additions: `.channel-command-preview` (faded italic monospaced, `-webkit-line-clamp: 2` cap), `.command-log-shell-partial` (max-height 240 px scrollable, `:empty { display: none }` so the pre collapses pre-first-chunk).

**Phase 4 setting + toast (HS-7984).** New DB-backed per-project setting `shell_streaming_enabled: boolean` (default `true`) added to `AppSettings` + `DEFAULT_SETTINGS` in `state.tsx`, hydrated by `settingsLoader.tsx::loadSettings` from the existing `/api/settings` payload. Settings UI: new `#settings-shell-streaming-enabled` checkbox in Settings → Experimental → Custom Commands section (placed there because that's where users configure shell commands; there's no dedicated Commands tab today). Wired in `settingsDialog.tsx`: dialog-open populates the checkbox from `state.settings.shell_streaming_enabled`, `change` handler PATCHes `/settings` and updates state. Both consumers gate on the setting: `attachShellPreviewToButton`'s `onPartial` returns early when off (also skipping the first-use toast); `applyShellPartialEvent` returns early when off. Server still buffers + dispatches events when off so re-enabling mid-run picks up at the next chunk. New exported `maybeFireShellStreamFirstUseToast()` helper fires the `Shell command output now streams as it arrives — Settings → Experimental to disable.` 7 s toast on the very first event after enable; `localStorage["hotsheet:shell-stream-toast-dismissed"]` sentinel ensures it shows at most once per browser ever. 6 new happy-dom tests cover toast first-fire / idempotence / respect-prior-sentinel / no-op-when-disabled + setting-gate apply / no-op for the Commands Log live render.

**Out of scope.** Streaming over PTY-style channels (the embedded terminal already handles interactive case). Colored ANSI rendering in the sidebar preview (Phase 3 strips ANSI — full xterm.js / Anser-like rendering is a separate ticket if requested). Cross-session resume — if a user reloads mid-command the partial buffer is lost; the completed log entry is still written on `child.close`.

**Cross-refs:** §15 (custom shell commands), §14 (Commands Log — Phase 3 sink), §22 (terminal — alternative path for interactive commands).

---

## 54. Global terminal checkout (`54-terminal-checkout.md`)

HS-7969 follow-up. New client module `src/client/terminalCheckout.tsx` owns one xterm.js instance per `(projectSecret, terminalId)` keyed map. Every consumer (drawer pane, dashboard tile + dedicated, drawer-grid tile + dedicated, quit-confirm preview pane) calls `checkout({projectSecret, terminalId, cols, rows, mountInto, onBumpedDown, onRestoredToTop})` to claim the terminal and gets back a `release()` handle. **LIFO stack** — most recent caller renders the live xterm in their `mountInto`; previous callers' mounts swap to a plain `Terminal in use elsewhere` placeholder; `release()` of the top hands the live xterm back to the next-most-recent caller (firing `onRestoredToTop`). Resize is **skipped when cols/rows match the previous owner** so TUI programs don't see SIGWINCH on every same-size handoff. **Empty stack disposes the xterm and closes the WebSocket** — the PTY survives on the server (other subscribers may exist; the per-project always-on session is independent), and the next `checkout()` re-creates the xterm + re-attaches + relies on the existing server-side scrollback replay (`src/terminals/registry.ts::attach` returns `history`; the WebSocket handler writes it before live data) to reproduce the previous visual state.

**Why.** Today the drawer pane is the only place that holds a client-side xterm instance per terminal-id; the dashboard / drawer-grid surfaces DOM-reparent the same instance from the drawer mount via `terminalTileGrid.tsx`, which works for the active project but doesn't generalise across projects. The §37 quit-confirm dialog spans every project, so its preview pane has been stuck on a static ANSI-spans render (HS-7969 follow-up #2) — visually close but not pixel-identical to the real terminal, and the user judged the gap unacceptable. The checkout module unifies all six consumers behind one mount semantic + lets the dashboard's existing virtualization (HS-6272 / HS-7825 / HS-7968) reclaim memory when no consumer is rendering a given terminal.

**Locked decisions** (2026-04-30 user feedback): (1) skip resize when cols/rows match; (2) plain placeholder ("Terminal in use elsewhere"), not a frozen ANSI snapshot — the snapshot can't pixel-match xterm's canvas renderer so the static text is the unambiguous version; (3) quit-confirm preview is a real checkout (resize to 80×30, not the ANSI-spans path); (4) no auto-reclaim from a placeholder click — the user dismisses whatever pushed the new checkout; (5) lazy-never-spawned terminals don't appear in the quit-confirm list at all (§37 already filters); (6) virtualization fully disposes the xterm on empty stack — the next checkout re-attaches + replays scrollback; (7) two phases, not three.

**Phasing.** **Phase 1 (HS-8031)** ships `terminalCheckout.tsx` + placeholder rendering + virtualization + a debug-only `_inspectStackForTesting()` helper (test-build only). Pure infrastructure — no UI consumers wired, every existing surface keeps using its current code path. Coverage: unit tests for create / push / pop / dispose-on-empty / resize-skip-on-same-size / cross-project independence + Playwright that opens the dashboard, dedicated-views a tile, closes the dashboard, and asserts the drawer regains the live terminal without a placeholder flash. **Phase 2 (HS-8032)** migrates every consumer (drawer pane in `terminal.tsx`, dashboard tile + dedicated in `terminalDashboard.tsx` + `terminalTileGrid.tsx`, drawer-grid in `drawerTerminalGrid.tsx`, quit-confirm preview in `quitConfirm.tsx`) to checkout calls; deletes the §37 ANSI-spans preview path (`src/client/ansiSpans.ts`, `paintPreviewContent`, `paletteFromTheme`) and the `GET /api/terminal/scrollback-preview` route once the quit-confirm migration lands clean.

**Status:** **Phase 2 fully complete — every sub-ticket shipped.** Phase 1 (HS-8031) + Phase 2.1 (HS-8041) + Phase 2.2 (HS-8042 + HS-8048) + Phase 2.3 verification (HS-8043) + Phase 2.4 drawer pane migration (HS-8044) + Phase 2.5 cleanup (HS-8045 — §37 ANSI-spans preview path deleted). Phase 1 shipped `src/client/terminalCheckout.tsx`. **Phase 2.1 (HS-8041, 2026-04-30)** wired the **quit-confirm preview pane** as the first consumer per §54.6. **Phase 2.2 (HS-8042 + HS-8048, 2026-04-30)** migrated both the **dedicated-view path** (HS-8042, §54.7 — `enterDedicatedView` → `checkout(...)`, `exitDedicatedView` → `view.checkout.release()`, new `CheckoutHandle.fit` + `CheckoutHandle.resize`, resize-first-write history-frame handling) AND the **tile preview path** (HS-8048, §54.8 — `mountTileXterm` + `connectTileSocket` collapsed into single `mountTileViaCheckout`, `tile.term`/`tile.ws`/`tile.xtermRoot` replaced with `tile.checkout`, per-consumer xterm config unified to checkout's defaults, `onRestoredToTop` re-applies CSS scaling, virtualization integration via `release()`, hidden HS-8042 keystroke regression closed by moving `term.onData` into checkout's WS handler). Result: opening a dedicated view for a terminal that already has a tile checkout pushes the tile down via the LIFO stack and reuses the SAME xterm — no longer creates 2 xterms. Memory savings scale with `(projects × terminals × dedicated-time)`. 7 new unit tests across `terminalCheckout.test.ts` (+2: `fit` exposure, `resize` semantics; 19/19) and `terminalTileGrid.test.ts` (+5 new file: rebuild-creates-entry / non-alive-skips / dispose-returns-zero / rebuild-disposes-old-mounts-new / cross-project-independence; 5/5). **Phase 2.3 (HS-8043) reduced to verification** — `terminalDashboard.tsx` uses the same shared `mountTileGrid()` so the dashboard automatically inherits the migration. **Phase 2.4 (HS-8044, 2026-04-30) drawer pane migration shipped** — `mountXterm` + `connect` collapsed into `mountInstanceViaCheckout`; the per-instance `connect` + `scheduleReconnect` paths in `terminal.tsx` deleted entirely (module-driven reconnect now lives in `terminalCheckout.tsx::attachWebSocketToEntry`); new `onControlMessage` callback on `CheckoutOptions` lets the drawer subscribe to parsed `'history'` / `'exit'` control messages without owning the WS; new `intentionallyClosing` flag distinguishes `release()` from network drop; `term.onData` registration moved to `createEntry` so it reads the live `entry.ws` reference dynamically (closes the hidden HS-8042 regression where keystrokes dispatched to the OLD dead WS after reconnect). **Phase 2.5 (HS-8045, 2026-04-30) cleanup shipped** — `src/client/ansiSpans.ts` + its test file deleted, `paintPreviewContent` / `paletteFromTheme` / `fetchScrollbackPreview` / `applyAppearanceToPreview` + their `void` references in `quitConfirm.tsx` deleted, `GET /api/terminal/scrollback-preview` route + `getTerminalScrollbackPreview` / `getTerminalScrollbackPreviewWithAnsi` registry helpers + `buildScrollbackPreview` / `buildScrollbackPreviewWithAnsi` snapshot helpers + their tests deleted. `stripAnsi` and `tailLines` in `scrollbackSnapshot.ts` retained (pure utility functions with existing test coverage). Every Phase 2 sub-ticket is now shipped — §54 is fully complete. **HS-8610 (2026-05-25, §54.12)** — fixed garbage (`?49;86R` / `3R3R`) appearing in the foreground program's input on tab switch: the replayed scrollback carries device-status QUERIES (`\x1b[?6n` DECXCPR etc.) that xterm auto-replies to via `onData`, and the reply was piped to the PTY as input. New per-entry `replaying` flag set around `applyHistoryReplay`'s write gates `term.onData`. 3 new tests.

**Out of scope.** Live placeholder painting (option (b) — fork-stream chunks to non-top consumers; revisit if a user complains about the static placeholder feeling wrong). Multi-instance for the same `(secret, terminalId)` (the server already supports multiple subscribers per session but the client-side single-instance assumption is baked in). Selection / search-state preservation across stack swaps (the live xterm is the same DOM node tree on reparent, so its own state follows naturally; the placeholder consumer has no meaningful "state" to preserve). OSC 133 jump-shortcut routing (continues to live in the OSC 133 module, keyed on terminal-id, unchanged by checkout).

**Cross-refs:** §22 (drawer pane consumer), §25 (dashboard tile + dedicated consumers), §36 (drawer-grid consumers), §37 (quit-confirm preview consumer + the path being deleted), §53 (independent — Commands Log streaming, no relation), HS-7969 (parent ticket — see also HS-7969 Notes for the back-and-forth that drove the locked decisions).

---

## 59. Reader-mode note navigation (`59-reader-note-navigation.md`)

HS-8233. Adds chevron-up (`previous`) / chevron-down (`next`) buttons to the §49 reader-mode overlay header so the user can step through every non-empty note on a ticket without re-clicking the per-note book icon for each. ArrowUp / ArrowDown also navigate. Buttons are disabled at list boundaries (no wrap-around).

**API.** New optional `navigation: { entries: ReaderEntry[]; initialIndex: number }` slot on `OpenReaderOverlayOptions` in `src/client/readerOverlay.tsx`. When omitted (the existing Details-reader path), the buttons aren't rendered and the overlay behaves exactly as it did pre-HS-8233. When provided, the active entry is the source of truth — overlay derives title + body from `entries[index]` on initial paint and on every navigation step. `initialIndex` is clamped to `[0, entries.length)` defensively.

**Wiring.** `noteRenderer.tsx`'s `.note-reader-btn` click handler + `app.tsx::bindDetailReaderButton` both build the navigation list at click time via `buildCombinedReaderEntries` (HS-8429). Empty notes / empty Details are skipped (they don't have a reader button anyway). When the combined list has just one entry, `navigation` is omitted so the chevrons aren't rendered.

**SCSS.** New `.reader-mode-header-actions` flex cluster groups the chevrons + close X. The `.reader-mode-close, .reader-mode-prev, .reader-mode-next` rule shares hover treatment + a `:disabled` opacity-0.35-cursor-default styling.

**Status.** Shipped (HS-8233 2026-05-06; HS-8429 unified Details+Notes navigation 2026-05-18).

**HS-8429 (2026-05-18).** Both surfaces now build the unified `[Details, ...non-empty notes]` list via the new pure helper `buildCombinedReaderEntries({ticketNumber, ticketTitle, detailsMarkdown, notes})`. Details lands at index 0 when non-empty; non-empty notes follow in display order. Each entry carries a stable `id` (the literal string `'details'` or the note's id, with a synthetic `__no-id-<idx>` fallback) so the noteRenderer's initial-index lookup is stable across notes that share an undefined id. The Details reader's `initialIndex` is the position of the Details entry (typically 0); the note reader's `initialIndex` is the clicked note's position (+1 when Details is included). 9 pure-helper test cases + 3 end-to-end integration cases in `readerOverlay.test.ts` cover the combined-entries shape and the cross-boundary navigation. See §59.9 of the source doc for the full behavior matrix.

**Out of scope.** Wrap-around navigation. Cross-ticket navigation. Edit-in-reader (§49 stays read-only).

**Cross-refs.** §49 (parent reader-mode design; the §49.6 overlay shell HS-8233 extends).

---

## 60. Fine-grained reactivity primitive design (`60-reactivity-primitive.md`)

HS-8166. Follow-up to the HS-8165 investigation ("would Solid be a better option?"). HS-8165's verdict: don't migrate — the pain is manual rebuilds + ad-hoc state, not the JSX runtime. This doc is the design for the reactivity half of that fix.

**Approach.** Adopt `kerfjs ^0.8.0` (sister project at `~/Documents/kerf`, written by the Hot Sheet author) behind a thin `src/client/reactive.ts` re-export so the underlying lib is swappable. (Initial adoption was at `^0.3.1` under HS-8166; bumped to `^0.5.0` under HS-8316 on 2026-05-10, `^0.6.0` under HS-8364, and `^0.8.0` under HS-8444 on 2026-05-18 — every bump non-breaking for Hot Sheet's usage subset.) Kerf re-exports `signal`/`computed`/`effect`/`batch` verbatim AND ships `defineStore`/`resetAllStores` (the §61 deliverable) PLUS `mount`/`each`/`toElement`/`SafeHtml`/`raw`/`Fragment` (the §62 deliverable) — one dependency covers all three design-doc chains. Ship three keyed-binding helpers in `src/client/reactive-bind.ts`: `bindText(el, sig)` for `textContent`, `bindAttr(el, attr, sig)` for `setAttribute` (with boolean-false → remove), and `bindList(parent, sig<T[]>, key, render)` for keyed list reconciliation that replaces every `parent.replaceChildren(...rows.map(toElement))` rebuild. Each helper returns a `() => void` disposer the caller must invoke on unmount; an ESLint rule flags discarded return values to prevent listener leaks. (Original `@preact/signals-core` direct survey kept in §60.3 for context.)

**Migration plan.** Phase 1 (HS-8235) lands the primitive + helpers + a single trial migration (project tabs in `src/client/projectTabs.tsx`). Phase 2 (HS-8236) tackles high-traffic surfaces — ticket list, command log, terminals — each as its own sub-ticket (HS-8311 / HS-8312 / HS-8313 / HS-8314). Phase 3 (HS-8237) is opportunistic; not every one of the ~54 manual-rebuild callsites needs to convert, only the ones where auto-rebuild pays off.

**What stays the same.** `jsx-runtime.ts`, `toElement(<jsx />)`, server `pages.tsx`, `raw(html)`, the defensive 'JSX: DOM elements as children' throw, all existing JSX call sites — unchanged. Signals only decide WHEN to re-mount, not HOW.

**Status:** **Phase 1 shipped 2026-05-09 (HS-8235); Phase 2 sub-tickets HS-8312 / HS-8313 / HS-8314 shipped 2026-05-09 → 2026-05-10; Phase 3 (HS-8237) closed 2026-05-10 as effectively-discharged** — every high-frequency rebuild surface was covered under Phase 2 or remains owned by the queued §61 store migrations (HS-8239 ticket list, HS-8240 command log + projects / terminals / channel stores). Remaining `replaceChildren` / `innerHTML = ''` callsites are low-frequency dialog / settings / mode-switch surfaces that explicitly fit the "can stay imperative" carve-out. New tickets get filed if a manual-rebuild bug surfaces. The earlier §63 reactivity-demo plan (parallel `morphdom` + hand-rolled `defineStore` infrastructure at `src/client/reactivity/`, demo at `/_demo/reactivity`) was retired under HS-8315 in favour of kerf — kerf strictly subsumes §63's morphdom + hand-rolled store API. **Event-delegation track (HS-8541 kerf audit, 2026-05-27):** `delegate`/`delegateCapture` added to the `reactive.ts` re-export, then per-element listeners migrated to container `delegate()` across the four Settings row lists (HS-8614), `noteRenderer` (HS-8613), and 9 hand-rolled `closest()` sites (HS-8615); the `bindList`-preserve stale-closure investigation (HS-8616) found + fixed a real `ticketRow`/`columnView` external-update bug (HS-8652, via a `liveTicket(id)` re-fetch); and the HS-8613-unblocked `noteRenderer` `morph()` flip landed (HS-8651 — `replaceChildren` → `morph` with image-proxy-on-template + `data-morph-skip` in-progress-edit preservation, Chromium-verified by `e2e/notes-morph.spec.ts`). See `60-reactivity-primitive.md` §60.5 for the full track. Cross-refs: §61 (stores layered on top of this primitive — also shipped Phase 1 via kerf re-export), §62 (independent track; kerf's `toElement` already includes the SVG-namespace fix the original §62 plan cared about — re-evaluate scope), HS-8165 (origin investigation), §17 of `docs/ai/code-summary.md` (client bundle entry).

---

## 61. Composable testable stores design (`61-composable-stores.md`)

HS-8167. Layered convention on top of §60's signals primitive. Hard dependency on HS-8166 landing before any phase here can start.

**Problem.** Client state lives in three overlapping shapes: module-level globals in `src/client/state.tsx`, per-feature module-level maps (`dashboardState` / `drawerGridState` / `terminalState` after HS-8189 / HS-8222 / HS-8223 / HS-8224 bundled the per-file `let`s), and ad-hoc `subscribeTo*` helpers. Tests can't seam in cleanly, derivations are hand-coded, and lifetime / project-switch reset is per-feature.

**`defineStore({initial, actions})` factory.** Returns `{ state: ReadonlySignal<T>, actions, reset() }`. Three rules: state is read-only (consumers subscribe via `effect()`), actions are the only mutation surface, `reset()` always returns to `initial()`. A module-level registry tracks every store; new `resetAllStores()` hook fires on `switchProject` so the per-feature reset hand-wiring goes away. Convention: one consumer = signal, two+ consumers (or multi-step mutations, or cross-navigation lifetime) = store.

**Candidate stores in pain order.** `ticketsStore` (highest impact — `loadTickets` / `setFilter` / `select` / `applyServerUpdate` / `removeTicket` / `optimisticUpdate` actions, derived `filtered` + `grouped` signals), `projectsStore`, `terminalsStore` (likely one store with derived per-surface views), `commandLogStore`, `channelStore` (consolidates state spread across `channelUI.tsx` + `permissionOverlay.tsx`).

**Migration plan.** Phase 1 (HS-8238) factory + project-tab attention-dot trial + written test pattern. Phase 2 (HS-8239 — atomic) `ticketsStore` end-to-end (with HS-8321 prep landing the factory + types + tests in isolation first to shrink the atomic-flip surface). Phase 3 (HS-8240) discharged 2026-05-10 into per-store sub-tickets: **HS-8317 (`projectsStore`) shipped 2026-05-10**; HS-8318 (`commandLogStore` + paired view-layer per the HS-8311 deferral) / HS-8319 (`terminalsStore`) / HS-8320 (`channelStore`) remain queued.

**Pre-implementation investigation rejected nanostores backbone (HS-8248).** Evaluated `nanostores` (~294 bytes core) as a drop-in for the bespoke `defineStore`. Rejected: nanostores' `.get()` doesn't auto-track via the `signal.value` getter protocol, so §60's `effect()`-based binding helpers can't consume nanostores without either parallel `bindTextNano` helpers OR a manual signal-mirror at every consumer — both reintroduce the "two reactivity systems" smell §60 + §61 exist to remove. Also: `cleanStores` semantics tear subscribers down (wrong shape for `resetAllStores` reset-to-initial), and the actions-only wrapper would be the bespoke factory regardless. Rationale archived in §61.13.

**Implementation update (HS-8235 / HS-8238 — 2026-05-09):** the local `defineStore` factory described in §61.3 was NOT implemented — kerf ships the same shape verbatim (read-only `state.value`, actions-only mutation, always-defined `reset()`, module-level registry walked by `resetAllStores()`). `src/client/reactive.ts` re-exports `defineStore` / `resetAllStores` / `Store` from `kerfjs`. Production `resetAllStores()` wiring deferred — every store landed so far holds CROSS-project state (attention dots) that shouldn't reset on switch; re-evaluate during HS-8239 (`ticketsStore` IS per-project and would be the natural first production caller).

**Status:** **Phase 1 shipped 2026-05-09 (HS-8238). HS-8240 (Phase 3 umbrella) closed 2026-05-10 as discharged into per-store sub-tickets HS-8317 / HS-8318 / HS-8319 / HS-8320; HS-8321 added as prep for HS-8239.** Phase 2 (HS-8239) itself still queued pending HS-8321 (the factory + types prep that shrinks the atomic-flip surface). Cross-refs: §60 (HS-8166 signals primitive — shipped Phase 1 alongside this), §62 (independent; kerf's `toElement` already covers the SVG-namespace bug class — re-scope), HS-8165 (origin), HS-8189 / HS-8190 / HS-8222 / HS-8223 / HS-8224 (prior `let`-bundling work this doc takes the next step on), §18 (plugin-defined stores deferred per §61.8).

---

## 62. Unified JSX render targets via shared AST design (`62-unified-jsx-render-targets.md`)

HS-8168. Independent of §60 and §61. Addresses the third "honest pain point" HS-8165 called out: server `SafeHtml` vs client `toElement(<jsx />)` divergence. Both emit ostensibly equivalent output, but `el.innerHTML = jsx.toString()` round-trips break subtly on SVG namespacing, attribute escape edge cases, custom attributes (`is`, `slot`, `xlink:href`, parser-quirky `<table>` / `<select>` content), and whitespace.

**Two options.** Option A — regression-test harness against the existing dual-target architecture (~50-case corpus; incremental, low-risk, but doesn't actually fix the bug class — only catches divergences we think to test for). Option B — unified runtime emitting an internal `JsxNode` AST + two consumers: `astToHtml` (server, today's semantics) + `astToDom` (client, builds DOM directly via `createElementNS` for SVG, `setAttribute` for attrs, `appendChild` for children — no `innerHTML` round-trip). **Original verdict: Option B.** Higher upfront cost (~1.5–2 days) but permanently closes the bug class, and the dual-consumer shape is the more interesting open-source artifact.

**Re-scope under HS-8315 (2026-05-09).** Post-kerf-adoption, the much simpler path is to route Hot Sheet's `toElement` through `kerfjs::toElement`, which already implements the SVG-namespace fix (the bug class §62 cared about) — same `SVG_FRAGMENT_TAGS` set, same `DOMParser('image/svg+xml')` for SVG fragments, same `<template>.innerHTML` fallback for HTML — byte-for-byte equivalent for HTML JSX. **Phase 1 (HS-8241) shipped 2026-05-09.** `src/client/dom.ts::toElement` is now a thin `(jsx) => kerfToElement(jsx.toString()) as HTMLElement` wrapper; the 244 existing call-sites are unchanged. 5 new SVG bug-class tests in `dom.test.tsx` (renamed from `.ts`). Phase 2 (HS-8242 — original "flip toElement to astToDom" plan) merged into Phase 1 since the same swap fulfilled both. **Phase 3 (HS-8243) shipped 2026-05-10 in reduced form** — `no-restricted-syntax` lint rule against direct `xxx.innerHTML = yyy` assignments + file-path allowlist for the 35 production client files (~93 callsites total) that already use the pattern; tests exempt via `**/*.test.{ts,tsx}` glob. New files / new code outside the allowlist trip the rule; existing usage migrates opportunistically on-touch. CLAUDE.md gained a sibling bullet to the `toElement` rule documenting the new convention. Full migration of the 93 existing callsites stays out of scope (multi-day refactor with real regression risk).

**AST shape.** `JsxNode { tag, props, children }` with `JsxChild = JsxNode | string | { __raw: string } | null | undefined | false | true`. Plain string children auto-escape; `raw(html)` produces `{__raw}` markers (the only `innerHTML` use in the new runtime, scoped to the explicit raw escape hatch). `JsxNode.toString()` calls `astToHtml(this)` so every existing server `SafeHtml.toString()` callsite is unchanged.

**Migration plan.** Phase 1 (HS-8241) lands the AST + `astToHtml` parity + `astToDom` skeleton + 50-case equivalence harness; `toElement` keeps using `innerHTML` so the new path is validated in isolation. Phase 2 (HS-8242) flips `toElement` to call `astToDom` directly when handed a `JsxNode`; full e2e + bundle-size gate. Phase 3 (HS-8243) wires the equivalence corpus into CI + lint rule warning on direct `innerHTML =` outside the explicit allowlist.

**What stays the same.** JSX surface (`<div>`), `SafeHtml` API, `raw(html)`, all call sites, server `pages.tsx`, the HS-6341 / HS-6342 'DOM-children-throw' defensive guard. Unchanged.

**Status:** Design only. Cross-refs: §60 / §61 (independent tracks — no dependency either direction), HS-8165 (origin), HS-6341 / HS-6342 (defensive throw preserved), §17 of `docs/ai/code-summary.md` (JSX runtime + bundle entry).

## 63. MCP tools for AI agents (`63-mcp-tools.md`)

HS-8344 design. Note: this slot was previously occupied by the retired reactivity-demo plan (HS-8315); the new occupant is unrelated.

`src/channel.ts` is already an MCP server registered in `.mcp.json` when the Claude Channel is enabled (§12), but it only exposes outbound notifications (`claude/channel` worklist events, `claude/channel/permission_request`). It defines **zero MCP tools** — every Claude → Hot Sheet operation today (status update, ticket create, completion signal, attachment upload, FEEDBACK NEEDED note) is a `curl` against the REST API documented in §9. The curl pattern has four specific failure modes: shell-escape pain on note bodies (backticks, dollar signs, quotes, newlines), wrong-instance routing in multi-project setups (HS-8340 was caused by exactly this), no type safety on free-form `category` / `priority` / `status` strings, and a ~120 prompt + ~80 response token cost per call vs ~30/30 for an MCP tool call.

**Design.** Add `tools/list` + `tools/call` handlers to `src/channel.ts` exposing 14 tools under the `hotsheet_` prefix: `update_ticket` / `create_ticket` / `get_ticket` / `delete_ticket` / `restore_ticket` / `toggle_up_next` / `duplicate_tickets` / `batch` / `edit_note` / `delete_note` / `add_attachment` / `signal_done` / `request_feedback` (sugar that prepends `FEEDBACK NEEDED:` / `IMMEDIATE FEEDBACK NEEDED:`) / `query_tickets`. Each tool internally proxies to the local Hot Sheet HTTP API using `port` + `secret` from `<dataDir>/settings.json` so there's no duplicated handler tree — Zod validation, markdown sync triggers, change-version bumping, attachment-backup hashing all live in one place. Soft-cutover migration: worklist + `hs-*` skills list MCP form first, curl form right below as fallback for non-Claude AI agents (Cursor, Aider) and human terminal callers.

**Phasing.** Phase 1 (HS-8346) — 5-tool core (`update_ticket` / `create_ticket` / `signal_done` / `add_attachment` / `request_feedback`) + tool-handler infrastructure + version bumps + new `src/channel.tools.test.ts`. Phase 2 (HS-8347) — remaining 9 tools. Phase 3 (HS-8348) — worklist template + 8 `hs-*` skill files rewritten to the two-form layout. Phase 4 (HS-8349) — multi-project tool naming via slug-suffix on server name, deferred until a user trips over collision. Phase 5 (HS-8350) — doc rollout into §12.13, §9.0, code-summary, requirements-summary in lockstep with Phase 1.

**Deliberately not exposed.** `GET /api/tickets` (list), `GET /api/tags`, stats / dashboard / settings / backups / projects / channel-management / gitignore / glassbox. The worklist file already gives the agent everything it needs; surfacing `list_tickets` trains agents to bypass the worklist. Agents that genuinely need these endpoints can curl them through the documented fallback path.

**Status:** Shipped — all five phases live (Phases 1 + 2 + 5 on 2026-05-12; Phase 4 on 2026-05-13; Phase 3 worklist+skills two-form rewrite landed alongside Phase 1). **HS-8346 (Phase 1) shipped:** `src/channel.tools.ts` exposes 5 tools (`update_ticket` / `create_ticket` / `signal_done` / `add_attachment` / `request_feedback`) via `tools/list` + `tools/call` handlers in `src/channel.ts`. **HS-8347 (Phase 2) shipped:** 9 additional tools live (`get_ticket` / `delete_ticket` / `restore_ticket` / `toggle_up_next` / `duplicate_tickets` / `batch` / `edit_note` / `delete_note` / `query_tickets`) — full 14-tool surface now. Each tool validates per-tool Zod input (reusing `TicketPrioritySchema` + `TicketStatusSchema` enums from `src/routes/validation.ts`), proxies to the local Hot Sheet HTTP API via `port` + `secret` from `<dataDir>/settings.json`, and returns the response body verbatim. **49 unit tests** in `src/channel.tools.test.ts` cover every tool × every error branch (validation rejection, HTTP error, network error, missing settings, note-id URL encoding, multi-field payload shapes for `batch` / `query_tickets`) without a live server. `CHANNEL_VERSION` + `EXPECTED_CHANNEL_VERSION` now 7 (HS-8346 → 5, HS-8347 → 6, HS-8349 → 7). **HS-8350 (Phase 5) shipped:** doc rollout into §12.13 of `docs/12-claude-channel.md` + `MCP tool equivalents` callout at the top of §9 of `docs/9-api.md` + this requirements-summary entry + `docs/ai/code-summary.md` `src/channel.ts` row + §17 reverse-index entry (and post-HS-8347 the 14-tool count + 49-test count). **HS-8349 (Phase 4) shipped 2026-05-13:** the channel server's MCP `Server({name})` and the `.mcp.json` registration key are now per-project — `hotsheet-channel-<slug>` where the slug is derived from the basename of the project root via `slugifyDataDir(dataDir)` in `src/channel-config.ts`. Multi-project Claude Code sessions can now distinguish each project's tools in the agent's tool list (`mcp__hotsheet-channel-<slug>__hotsheet_update_ticket`). `registerChannel` opportunistically migrates any legacy `hotsheet-channel` entry on the same `.mcp.json`; `unregisterChannel` cleans both keys. The `claude --dangerously-load-development-channels server:hotsheet-channel-<slug>` command is built by `claudeWithChannelCommand(dataDir)` in `src/terminals/resolveCommand.ts` and surfaced via the new `serverName` field on `GET /api/channel/status`; Settings → Experimental renders the per-project command via `experimentalSettings.tsx`. Pulled forward from the deferred queue on user direction that multi-project support is load-bearing rather than polish. Cross-refs: §9 (REST API — universal interface, source of truth for validation), §12 (Claude Channel — host environment for the MCP server), HS-8340 (multi-project routing bug the curl pattern caused), CLAUDE.md `CHANNEL_VERSION` convention.

## 67. Claude Code OpenTelemetry integration (`67-telemetry.md`)

Foundations + opt-in stack shipped 2026-05-20 (7 of 15 tickets, including the HS-8470 persistence follow-up filed in-flight). **HS-8684 (2026-05-28) reversed the original opt-in default to default-on** — `telemetry_enabled === undefined` (no choice yet) is now treated as enabled by both the spawn-env gate (`otelEnv.ts`) and the visibility gate (`telemetry.ts::anyProjectHasTelemetryEnabled`); only an explicit `false` opts out. Rationale: the OTLP receiver is localhost-bound + `hotsheet_project`-filtered (§67.5.3), so the "user should consent before any of that happens" framing was protecting against an off-machine leak the architecture already prevents. Hot Sheet captures [Claude Code's OTLP signals](https://code.claude.com/docs/en/monitoring-usage.md), persists them locally to PGLite, and surfaces them as per-project cost chips + analytics-dashboard rollups + per-prompt drilldowns + cross-project dashboards.

**Receiver topology decision (§67.4):** same-port — `POST /v1/metrics` + `/v1/logs` + `/v1/traces` live on the existing Hono server (NOT under `/api/*` so the `X-Hotsheet-Secret` middleware doesn't reject Claude Code's bundled exporter). Sibling-port topology reserved for future scale; `telemetry_receiver_port_override` in `~/.hotsheet/settings.json` is the forward-compat hook (unused in current implementation).

**Foundations (HS-8142 + HS-8144 + HS-8143):** doc landed `docs/67-telemetry.md` (14 sections incl. the 14-ticket map at §67.14). Three new PGLite tables — `otel_metrics` / `otel_events` / `otel_spans` — each with JSONB attribute bags + `(project_secret, ts DESC)` rollup indexes + `(session_id, ts)` drilldown indexes + (events + spans) `(prompt_id)` for the per-prompt timeline modal. `SCHEMA_VERSION` bumped 2 → 3 per §41 / §45. Receiver routes accept protobuf + JSON, return `200 OK` empty body; JSON payloads are parsed end-to-end.

**Opt-in stack → opt-out stack (HS-8470 + HS-8145 + HS-8146 + HS-8154; HS-8684 flipped the default):** JSON payloads are persisted via `src/db/otelWriters.ts` (`persistMetricsPayload` / `persistLogsPayload` / `persistTracesPayload`) which drop entries whose `hotsheet_project` resource-attribute isn't a registered project (the §67.5.3 anti-pollution gate, via `getProjectBySecret`). Spawn-env injection lives in `src/terminals/registry/otelEnv.ts::buildOtelEnv(dataDir)` — reads per-project `telemetry_*` settings, returns the env block when `telemetry_enabled !== false` (HS-8684 default-on; `undefined` and `true` both enable, only explicit `false` opts out), wired into `lifecycle.ts::buildEnv`. Settings → Telemetry tab (new in `pages.tsx` + `bindTelemetryTab()` in `settingsDialog.tsx`) hosts the master toggle + per-signal sub-toggles + retention picker; PATCH `/api/file-settings` per change. Retention sweep (`cleanupTelemetryRows(dataDir)` in `src/cleanup.ts`) runs at server startup alongside the existing `cleanupAttachments` — DELETE rows past `telemetry_retention_days` (default 30, `0` = forever) from all three tables.

**Phase 2b protobuf decode (HS-8471, shipped):** `protobufjs` runtime + inline OTLP `.proto` schema strings in `src/routes/otlpProtos.ts` + decoder in `src/routes/otelDecoder.ts::decodeProtobufPayload(signalType, bytes)`. Both wire formats normalize to the same JSON-shape object the writers consume — `trace_id` / `span_id` / `parent_span_id` converted from base64 (protobufjs default) to lowercase hex (OTLP/JSON convention) so storage is consistent across wire formats. Closed the user-visible gap: a `claude` run with telemetry on now produces `[otel] … inserted=N dropped=0` stdout lines and rows in PGLite (vs the previous `inserted=0` placeholder).

**Drawer Telemetry tab (HS-8148, shipped):** the first UI surface that consumes the persisted rows. `GET /api/telemetry/drawer?scope=project|all` returns the full `DrawerPayload` (today/week/all-time `WindowTotals` chips + by-model + by-tool + by-query-source rollups + 50 recent prompts) via live queries in `src/db/otelQueries.ts`; no precomputed views per §67.6. Client surface in `src/client/telemetryDrawer.tsx` with `loadAndRenderTelemetryDrawer` (lazy-imported by `commandLog.tsx::switchDrawerTab` when the user activates the tab) and `initTelemetryDrawer` (one-time scope-toggle + recent-prompt-row click delegation, wired from `app.tsx`). New drawer tab + content panel added in `pages.tsx` between Commands Log and the dynamic terminal tabs. Empty-state shows a "Enable telemetry in Settings → Telemetry, then run `claude` in a Hot Sheet terminal" prompt for users who haven't opted in or whose Claude Code hasn't exported yet.

**Per-project today-cost surface (HS-8147 shipped → HS-8527 relocated 2026-05-22):** originally a `.project-tab-cost` pill in every project-tab header; under HS-8527 the chip was retired in favor of an inline cost element in the **sidebar dashboard widget** (right-aligned next to "N in progress"), AND the widget itself was moved up the sidebar to sit directly under `#sidebar-git-chip` rather than at the bottom (after `#stats-bar`). Hidden when today's cost is zero AND under subscription billing (HS-8497). `GET /api/telemetry/today-cost-by-project` returns `{ costs: { [secret]: number } }` keyed by project secret; `src/client/costPoll.tsx::initCostPoll` subscribes to the existing bell-state long-poll cadence (`bellPoll.subscribeToBellState`) so refreshes piggyback on the existing tick — no new timer. `dashboardMode.tsx::updateSidebarWidgetCost(costs)` filters down to the active project's secret + writes into `.sidebar-widget-cost`; `refreshSidebarWidgetCost()` re-applies the cached map after the widget is re-mounted on project switch (no blank between re-mount + next bell tick). Clicking the widget itself still enters the analytics dashboard for the active project; the cost element is non-interactive (HS-8527 dropped the chip's click-to-dashboard handler since the parent widget already carries that behavior).

**Per-tool latency histograms (HS-8150, shipped):** New section in the drawer Telemetry tab between "By tool" and "By query source." For each tool the user has invoked, an inline-SVG bar chart shows the latency distribution across 8 logarithmic buckets (<10ms, 10-50ms, 50-100ms, 100-500ms, 500ms-1s, 1-5s, 5-10s, 10s+) plus p50/p90/p99 percentile labels in the header. Backend `getToolLatencyHistogram` uses PostgreSQL `percentile_cont WITHIN GROUP (ORDER BY (attributes_json->>'duration_ms')::numeric)` for percentiles + a second `GROUP BY tool, CASE` query to bucket counts; bundled into `getDrawerPayload.toolLatencyHistogram` so the drawer's existing single-fetch refreshes the section alongside the rest. No chart-library dep — just `<rect>` bars sized proportionally to the max bucket count with `currentColor` fill. Source = `claude_code.tool_result.attributes.duration_ms` (events-based, always-on); `otel_spans`-based variant deferred until traces (HS-8155) ships if richer per-span breakdowns matter.

**Correlation + per-ticket rollup (HS-8151 + HS-8152, shipped):** HS-8151 investigation picked Option 3 (marker injection in the channel-trigger flow) over the four alternatives — env injection at spawn was too static, MCP context had the same staleness issue, time-window heuristics were ambiguous. HS-8152 implements: client-side, `triggerChannelAndMarkBusy` in `channelUI.tsx` calls `tagMessageWithActiveTicket(message)` which prepends `<!-- hotsheet:ticket=HS-NNNN -->\n\n` when there's an active ticket — the marker rides into `claude_code.user_prompt`'s body verbatim. Server-side, `getPerTicketRollup(ticketNumber)` in `src/db/otelQueries.ts` LIKE-matches the marker in `body_json::text`, joins on `prompt_id` against `api_request` events to sum cost + tokens, computes total duration as `SUM(MAX(ts) - MIN(ts))` per prompt. New endpoint `GET /api/telemetry/ticket/:number`. UI: `src/client/ticketTelemetryStats.tsx::loadAndRenderTicketTelemetry(ticketNumber)` renders a "Claude usage on this ticket" stats grid inside the detail panel (`#detail-telemetry-stats`); hidden when `promptCount === 0` to keep the panel uncluttered for unused tickets. Wired from `detail.tsx::loadDetail` post meta-info paint. **HS-8730 (2026-06-04) — time-window correlation added (fixes HS-8729 "most tickets show no cost"):** the marker alone only tagged the one detail-panel-open ticket at channel-trigger time, so the agentic worklist flow (Claude pulls tickets off Up Next + marks each started→completed) left most tickets un-attributed. New `src/db/ticketWorkIntervals.ts` + `ticket_work_intervals` table (telemetry DB, `project_secret`-keyed, SCHEMA_VERSION 4→5) record real `[started, ended]` work windows from the `updateTicket` status-transition hook; `getPerTicketRollup(ticketNumber, secret?)` UNIONs the marker path with a time-window path (api_request `ts` ∈ interval), deduped at event level; `POST /channel/done` closes open intervals. Now essentially every ticket Claude works gets its real cost. Honest limits: work with no `started` ticket stays project-only; concurrent same-project sessions can cross-attribute by time (rare). **Storage decision:** marker stays parse-at-query LIKE; intervals are an indexed table.

**Per-prompt timeline drilldown (HS-8149, shipped):** click any row in the drawer Telemetry tab's recent-prompts list → opens a 90vw/90vh modal via `src/client/promptDrilldown.tsx::openPromptDrilldown(promptId)`. Modal chrome mirrors `readerOverlay.tsx` (close button + Escape + backdrop click). `GET /api/telemetry/prompt/:id` returns the `PromptTimeline` shape — every `otel_events` row matching `prompt_id`, sorted by ts ASC, with first/last ts + best-effort model extraction. Body renders a vertical timeline; each row's button-as-header shows ts + relative-from-first + event name with a color-coded badge (`telemetry-event-prompt` / `-api` / `-error` / `-tool` / `-decision` / `-other`). Click any row → toggles `aria-expanded` + reveals a `<pre>` block with `attributes_json` + `body_json` formatted via `JSON.stringify(…, 2)` for debugging. Empty-entries timeline (unknown prompt id) renders a friendly message instead of erroring.

**Spawn-env contract (§67.3):** when `telemetry_enabled !== false` per-project (HS-8684 default-on), Hot Sheet's terminal-spawn injects `CLAUDE_CODE_ENABLE_TELEMETRY=1` + `OTEL_METRICS_EXPORTER=otlp` + `OTEL_LOGS_EXPORTER=otlp` + `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_PROTOCOL=http/protobuf` + `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT=http://localhost:<port>` + `OTEL_RESOURCE_ATTRIBUTES=hotsheet_project=<secret>,working_dir=<dataDir>`. Beta tracing adds `OTEL_TRACES_EXPORTER=otlp` + `CLAUDE_CODE_ENHANCED_TELEMETRY_BETA=1` when `telemetry_traces_enabled === true`.

**Cross-project dashboard + beta-traces design (HS-8153 + HS-8155, design-only):** the last two §67 tickets each have a dedicated requirements doc — `docs/68-telemetry-traces.md` (beta enhanced tracing + span-tree + inline waterfall) and `docs/69-telemetry-dashboard.md` (cross-project dashboard with conditional sidebar entry + 7×24 heatmap + top-10 prompts). Each doc decomposes into ~4–5 implementation follow-up tickets (HS-8475 through HS-8478 for traces; HS-8479 through HS-8483 for the dashboard). Design decisions resolved: span tree replaces flat events when present (one canonical hierarchy, not two parallel surfaces); waterfall lives inline at the top of the drilldown body (collapsible `<details>`, single overlay, click-bar-scrolls-tree); dashboard sidebar entry is conditional on `telemetry_enabled === true` in at least one project (no flicker, single inflection point); heatmap is 7×24 day-of-week × hour grid (richer signal than a 24-hour bar). The HS-8479…8483 sub-tickets shipped 2026-05-21.

**Telemetry surface reshape (HS-8503, design-only 2026-05-21):** user feedback drove a consolidation pass: the cross-project surface moved from a conditional sidebar entry to a **header-bar icon** (line-chart Lucide glyph, next to `#terminal-dashboard-toggle`); the drawer Telemetry tab + the per-prompt drilldown's "Recent prompts" list both moved to the **analytics dashboard** (per-project telemetry sections appended below the existing throughput / cycle-time / category-breakdown charts); a new shared **cost-over-time stacked-area chart** with Stacked / Overlay (per-project) modes lives on both surfaces; the cross-project "Top 10 most expensive prompts" list was removed (replaced by "10 most recent prompts" on the per-project analytics dashboard). Reshape spec lives in §69.10 of `docs/69-telemetry-dashboard.md`; §67.10.1 / .10.2 / .10.5 / .10.6 in `docs/67-telemetry.md` are annotated with supersession pointers. ## 72. Memory-primary snapshot persistence (`72-snapshot-persistence.md`)

HS-8575 investigation. Answers the user's standing ask — *DB gets corrupted fairly regularly even on clean shutdown; can it run in-memory and persist atomically?* **Yes, and the machinery already exists.** Today's file-backed mode (`new PGlite('<dataDir>/db')`) keeps a full multi-file PostgreSQL cluster live on disk; corruption is endemic because those files must stay mutually consistent and a crash mid-update (or the HS-7932 fsync-no-op window) leaves them inconsistent. Every shipped mitigation (graceful close HS-7931, fsync wrap HS-7935, stale-pid removal HS-7888, preserve-aside HS-7889, backups §7/§41, repair §42) is a defensive patch around an inherently fragile format — it can reduce frequency but not eliminate the class.

**Proposed architecture:** open PGLite **in-memory** (`new PGlite('memory://')`), seed at boot from the last-good snapshot via `{ loadDataDir: blob }`, and persist by `CHECKPOINT` → `db.dumpDataDir('gzip')` → single tarball written **atomically** (`tmp` + `fsync` + `rename`). The atomic rename means the on-disk artifact is only ever the complete old or complete new snapshot — **the corruption class becomes structurally impossible**, and the HS-7888 stale-pid class disappears (no pid file on disk). Triggers: debounced post-write (~1–2 s), final snapshot in `gracefulShutdown` (§45.3 hook point → zero loss on clean exit), periodic safety timer. **Reuses code Hot Sheet already ships + trusts:** `dumpDataDir('gzip')` (`backup.ts:185`), `loadDataDir` (`backup.ts:407`, `repair.ts:49`), atomic `tmp`+`sync`+`rename` (`dbJsonExport.ts:71`) — proven by the 2026-04-27 639/639-ticket restore.

**Honest trade-offs:** crash-loss window = writes since last snapshot (clean shutdown loses nothing; strictly better than today's 5-min-tier worst case + no more silent total corruption); whole DB in RAM (ticketing data tiny, but **§67 telemetry tables are the variable to measure** — high-volume + per-project + multiplied by registered projects); snapshot latency grows with data; **telemetry's continuous high-volume writes argue for splitting telemetry into a separate file-backed disposable DB** so the memory-primary store holds only durable user data. Backups (§7) get simpler (copy the canonical snapshot); Repair (§42) shrinks; the §44 WASM `pg_resetwal` spike can stay deferred indefinitely.

**Recommendation:** pursue it, phased + behind a `db_persistence_mode: 'file' | 'snapshot'` setting (default `'file'`), measure before any default flip. Phase 1 prototype + benchmark (RAM + snapshot latency incl. realistic telemetry, single/multi-project); Phase 2 snapshot triggers + SIGKILL crash-window harness; Phase 3 telemetry-split decision; Phase 4 migration + cutover.

**§72.6 RAM follow-up (HS-8575 comment):** user flagged that full in-memory may cost too much RAM. Audit of installed **PGLite 0.3.16** confirms the choice's real shape: `NodeFS extends EmscriptenBuiltinFilesystem` (NODEFS write-through) means **today's mode is already the low-RAM one** (pages to disk, doesn't hold the whole DB in RAM) — so full `memoryfs` would *increase* RAM. PGLite's four FS backends: `nodefs` (us, low-RAM/corruption-prone), `memoryfs` (full-RAM/atomic-snapshot), `idbfs` + `opfs-ahp` (**browser-only**). **The only journaled VFS PGLite ships (`opfs-ahp`, with a `WALEntry` op-log over a sync-access-handle pool) is browser-only and can't run in our Node/Tauri server.** `relaxedDurability` is a speed knob that *weakens* durability (wrong direction); `syncToFs` is a near no-op for `nodefs`. So no Node-side PGLite flag gives journaled-low-RAM-atomic durability — it must be built at our layer. Two middle-ground designs added to §72.6: **Option D** (filed as **HS-8583**) — keep low-RAM `nodefs` live but treat the atomic snapshot as the *trusted* artifact + **auto-restore** on open/integrity failure (corruption becomes non-fatal + self-healing at zero extra RAM; does NOT make it impossible); and **Option B′** — `memoryfs` for the *small* durable set only (tickets/attachments/settings) + `nodefs` for telemetry, which is corruption-proof for user data AND RAM-bounded (elevates the Phase-3/HS-8579 telemetry split to the recommended end-state). Updated rec: ship Option D first (cheapest robustness/RAM win), target Option B′ as end-state.

**Status:** Design + Phases 1 & 3 (benchmark + split decision) done; **Phases 2 & 4 (implementation) DROPPED — closed WON'T FIX 2026-05-25** (HS-8578 / HS-8580). The memory-primary track is abandoned: §73 (Option D, shipped) already makes corruption non-fatal + self-healing at zero extra RAM, so memory-primary's only remaining benefit (corruption-*proof* durable set) wasn't worth the ~+243 MB/project second-instance cost of the Option B′ telemetry split. The investigation (§72) stays as the record of why. **HS-8577 (Phase 1) shipped** — `scripts/bench-memory-primary.ts` measured RAM + dump latency on realistic telemetry, single + multi-project (results in §72.7). Findings: the WASM Postgres baseline is ~840 MB/instance (mode-independent, ~+243 MB per additional instance); with 200k telemetry events memory-primary costs **+915 MB RSS / +2.1 GB WASM** over file-backed, and the whole-cluster dump hits **~6.2 s / 76 MB** — so naive whole-cluster memory-primary is NOT viable with telemetry on. **HS-8579 (Phase 3) decision = GO on Option B′ (telemetry split)** — §72.8 records the decision + implementation sketch. Audit confirmed it's low-risk: **zero cross-DB JOINs** between `otel_*` and durable tables, blast radius = 3 modules (`otelWriters.ts` / `otelQueries.ts` / `cleanupTelemetryRows`) all already resolving via context-based `getDb()`, and `dbJsonExport.ts` already excludes otel. Sketch: a lazily-opened second `getOtelDb()` → `<dataDir>/db-otel/` (file-backed `nodefs`, disposable, opened only when `telemetry_enabled`), `initOtelSchema` split out, durable DB gets the memory-primary snapshot, telemetry DB is NOT snapshotted, migration is "start fresh" (telemetry disposable). The production `db_persistence_mode` setting + open-path (originally scoped into Phase 1) was deliberately NOT built — the naive global mode is the wrong shape. **Phase 2 (HS-8578, triggers + crash-window harness) and Phase 4 (HS-8580, migration + cutover) were closed WON'T FIX on 2026-05-25** — the memory-primary track is not being implemented, because §73 (Option D) already shipped and makes corruption non-fatal at zero RAM, leaving Option B′ only a corruption-PROOF upgrade whose ~+243 MB/project second-instance cost isn't justified. **Option D (HS-8583) was promoted to its own greenlit design doc — §73.** Cross-refs: §7 (dump/load path promoted to primary), §41 (JSON co-save kept), §42 (Repair shrinks), §44 (WASM resetwal can stay deferred), §45 (cleaner-shutdown stack this largely makes redundant; reuses the `gracefulShutdown` hook), §46 (snapshot mode simplifies the single-owner story), §73 (the low-RAM Option D, designed in full).

## 73. Snapshot Protection — NodeFS live + atomic snapshot + auto-restore (`73-snapshot-protection.md`)

HS-8583 — the **greenlit, low-RAM "Option D"** from §72.6, now its own design of record. Keeps today's on-disk `nodefs` live cluster exactly as-is (low RAM — `nodefs` already pages to disk, doesn't hold the whole DB in RAM) but **stops trusting it as the source of truth.** Independently shippable; does NOT require adopting `memoryfs`.

**The model.** Maintain one atomically-written canonical snapshot `<dataDir>/.hotsheet/snapshot.tar.gz` and **auto-restore from it** whenever the live cluster comes up broken. Snapshot production reuses the proven path: `CHECKPOINT` → `db.dumpDataDir('gzip')` → `tmp` + `handle.sync()` (fsync) + `rename` (the `writeJsonExportAtomically` pattern, `dbJsonExport.ts:71`). Triggers (gated on the setting): debounced ~2 s off the existing `scheduleAllSync` mutation signal (`src/sync/markdown.ts`); a final snapshot step added to `gracefulShutdown` (§45.3) → **zero loss on clean exit**; a dirty-gated 120 s safety floor. New module `src/db/snapshot.ts`, per-project dirty + in-progress guards mirroring `BackupState`.

**Startup recovery flow.** `getDbByPath` → open `db/` → **integrity probe** (`SELECT 1` + `SELECT count(*) FROM tickets` + catalog-corruption catch — §73.5) → on throw OR probe-fail → `restoreFromSnapshot()`: (1) preserve corrupt `db/` aside (HS-7889 rename), (2) pick newest good source in order — canonical `snapshot.tar.gz` → §7 `5min`→`hourly`→`daily` tier tarball that `loadDataDir`-validates (reuses the `src/routes/db.ts` "find a working backup" iterator), (3) `new PGlite(db/, { loadDataDir: blob })` into a fresh dir, (4) write the HS-7899 marker + emit toast/log, (5) no good source → today's empty-recreate + banner (unchanged). Preserve-aside always runs first, so auto-restore never destroys the corrupt cluster.

**Three confirmed decisions (asked up front):** **D1** dedicated fresh **local** snapshot inside `dataDir` (NOT the possibly-slow Google-Drive `backupDir`, HS-8174; §7 tiers stay the deeper fallback) → loss window ≤ seconds; **D2** **auto-restore + notify** (toast + command-log line, no blocking banner, zero clicks — the corrupt dir is kept for rescue); **D3** **on by default** — `db_snapshot_protection: true` per-project, Settings → Backups toggle to disable.

**Honest limitation.** Does NOT make corruption *impossible* (live files stay the fragile multi-file format) — makes it **non-fatal + self-healing** with seconds-bounded loss, at **zero extra RAM**. The corruption-*proof* guarantee is what §72's `memoryfs` buys at a RAM cost. Shipping Option D first de-risks §72 and its writer/atomic-write/auto-restore code is directly reusable there.

**Status:** Shipped (fully implemented). **HS-8586 (Phase 1)** — `src/db/snapshot.ts` writer + `db_snapshot_protection` setting + 3 triggers + 13 unit tests. **HS-8587 (Phase 2)** — integrity probe + auto-restore flow + §7-tier fallback + `restoredFrom`/`restoredTicketCount` marker + D2 success toast in `dbRecoveryBanner.tsx`. **HS-8594 (Settings UI, split from Phase 2)** — `src/client/snapshotProtectionUI.tsx` toggle + status line, `GET /api/db/snapshot-status` route, formatter unit tests + route round-trip test + `e2e/snapshot-protection.spec.ts` toggle-persistence e2e. **HS-8588 (Phase 3)** — SIGKILL crash-recovery e2e in `src/db/snapshotCrashRecovery.e2e.test.ts` on the new shared `src/spawnTestServer.ts` child-process harness (3 cases: bounded loss, snapshot-beats-backup precedence, multi-project isolation); the harness was extracted from the HS-7934 graceful-shutdown e2e, which now also uses it. Cross-refs: §72 (high-RAM corruption-proof sibling; §72.6 origin), §7 (deeper fallback + iterator reused), §42 (Repair complementary, mostly bypassed once self-heal lands), §45 (`gracefulShutdown` gains the final-snapshot step), HS-7889/HS-7899 (preserve-aside + marker promoted manual→automatic), HS-7932/HS-7935 (fsync finding + wrap reused).
