## 74. Clear Telemetry Data (`74-clear-telemetry-data.md`)

HS-8606 (shipped 2026-05-25). A manual "Clear telemetry data…" button in Settings → Telemetry → Retention (danger-styled, with an inline status line) that permanently deletes every `otel_metrics` / `otel_events` / `otel_spans` row for the **active project** (all time), complementing the automatic age-based retention sweep (§67.6). Useful for wiping inflated pre-HS-8599 cumulative rows, reclaiming space, or clearing before sharing a machine. Always available regardless of the `telemetry_enabled` master toggle.

**Flow.** Click → `confirmDialog({ danger: true })` (Tauri-safe overlay, cancel = no-op) → `DELETE /api/telemetry/project-data` (active secret in the `X-Hotsheet-Secret` header) → server `clearProjectTelemetry(projectSecret)` deletes `WHERE project_secret = ?` across all three otel tables with **no time filter**, via `getTelemetryDb()` (the shared telemetry DB, §67.6 / HS-8581) → `{ deleted }` drives the status line ("Cleared N telemetry rows." / singular / "No telemetry data to clear."). §70/§71 surfaces pick it up on their next 30 s poll.

**Post-clear UI fixes (HS-8620 / HS-8621 / HS-8622, shipped 2026-05-25).** (1) The sidebar cost widget is now **zeroed** for the active project via `dashboardMode.tsx::clearSidebarWidgetCostForActiveProject`, not merely refreshed: `refreshSidebarWidgetCost()` re-rendered the stale cached value because the HS-8531 sticky cache keeps showing the last cost for any project the next `today-cost-by-project` fetch omits — and a just-cleared project IS omitted (zero today), so the dollar value persisted until the next prompt. (2) The one-shot "Cleared N rows." status (`#settings-telemetry-clear-status`, a static reused element) is wiped on Settings-open via `resetClearTelemetryStatus()` so a prior project's count doesn't linger after a project switch. (3) The §70 cross-project "Cost by project" table labels an unresolved (closed/unregistered) project's secret as `Unknown project (<8-char prefix>)` (`resolveProjectName`) instead of the bare hex prefix. New tests in `sidebarWidgetCost.test.ts` (cost zeroing), `telemetryClearUI.test.tsx` (status reset), `crossProjectStatsPage.test.tsx` (name fallback). Known gap: a closed project's lingering rows still have no clear path — tracked as **HS-8625**.

**Safety.** Per-project only — the delete is always secret-scoped; the route returns `400` (and `clearProjectTelemetry` is never reached) when no secret resolves, so a misconfigured request can't wipe the shared store across every project. Permanent (no undo); touches only the three `otel_*` tables.

**Implementation.** `clearProjectTelemetry` in `src/db/otelQueries.ts`; `DELETE /api/telemetry/project-data` in `src/routes/telemetry.ts`; `src/client/telemetryClearUI.tsx` (`bindClearTelemetryButton` + pure `formatClearResult`) wired from `bindTelemetryTab` (`settingsDialog.tsx`); markup in `pages.tsx`; `.settings-inline-row` / `.settings-status` styles in `styles.scss`. Tests: per-secret scoped delete + no-op (`otelQueries.test.ts`), route count/scope/400 (`telemetry.test.ts`), formatter + confirm/success/error flow (`telemetryClearUI.test.tsx`), and E2E `e2e/clear-telemetry.spec.ts` (HS-8608 — OTLP-seed → button → real confirm overlay → "Cleared N…" status + server-side zero, plus cancel path).

**Status:** Shipped 2026-05-25. Cross-refs: §67.6 (automatic retention sweep — the complement), §67 "Single shared store" / HS-8581 (shared-DB routing), §70/§71 (telemetry surfaces that reflect the cleared state on next poll).

---

## 76. Cross-project ticket drag — copy / move (`76-cross-project-ticket-drag.md`)

HS-8663 (shipped 2026-06-05). Drag selected tickets from the list / column view onto **another project's tab** to copy them there, or hold **Option/Alt** to move them (recreate in target + soft-delete the originals). Dropping onto the always-tabbed strip's **"+" button** (§4.2 / HS-8664) opens the folder picker and transfers the tickets into the freshly-registered project; canceling the picker changes nothing. Mirrors keyboard copy/paste ≈ drag-copy and cut/paste ≈ Option-drag (§3), drag-driven.

**Implementation.** Drag sources (`ticketRow.tsx` / `columnView.tsx`) already publish dragged ids via `setDraggedTicketIds` (`ticketListState.ts`); their `dragstart` now sets `effectAllowed = 'copyMove'` (was `'move'`) so a tab drop can offer copy. `projectTabs.tsx` distinguishes a ticket drag (`dragSecret === null && draggedTicketIds.length > 0`) from a tab reorder, lights the hovered tab / "+" button with a single-slot `.drag-over` highlight (clears on `dragleave` / drop / a global `dragend`), sets `dropEffect` from `e.altKey`, and routes the drop to the shared `transferTicketsToProject` (`ticketTransfer.ts`). Dropping onto the **source project's own tab is a no-op**. The "+"-button drop threads a one-shot `onRegistered` callback through `showOpenFolderDialog` (`openFolder.tsx`) — run before the auto-switch so a move deletes from the still-active source; dropped on every cancel path. `transferTicketsToProject` recreates each ticket in the target (`createTicket(req, { secret })` — title/details/category/priority/status/up_next/tags, trashed→`not_started`), carries notes (`putTicketNotesBulk(id, notes, { secret })`), and for a move soft-deletes originals with the explicit **source** secret. `createTicket` + `putTicketNotesBulk` gained an optional `{ secret }` arg (matching `updateTicket`/`deleteTicket`). A toast confirms ("Copied/Moved N ticket(s) to <project>").

**Attachments (HS-8739, shipped 2026-06-05).** Both the drag (`transferTicketsToProject`) and the clipboard copy/cut/paste (`clipboard.ts::pasteTickets`) carry a ticket's attachments to the target via a new server endpoint `POST /api/tickets/:id/attachments/copy-from` (typed caller `copyTicketAttachments(targetId, { sourceSecret, sourceTicketId }, { secret })`). The server reads the source ticket's non-draft attachment rows from the source project's DB (`runWithDataDir`) and copies the files (absolute `stored_path`) into the target project's `attachments/` dir — no browser round-trip; duplicate target names suffixed, draft + missing-file rows skipped; best-effort (a copy failure is logged, the transfer still succeeds). Closes the prior move-loses-attachments gap. Tests: `src/routes/attachmentCopyCrossProject.test.ts` (route across two project DBs), `ticketTransfer.test.ts` (wiring + secrets), `api/attachments.test.ts` (caller + schema), and the §76 drag E2E (`copy carries attachments`).

**Tests.** Unit: `ticketTransfer.test.ts` (copy/move secrets, notes carry, trashed→not_started, source-secret delete) + `projectTabsTicketDrop.test.ts` (drop-onto-other-tab wiring, Option→move, no-op on own tab, reorder doesn't transfer). **E2E (HS-8740):** `e2e/cross-project-drag.spec.ts` registers a real second project (temp dir, unregistered in `afterEach`) and synthesizes the drag → copy lands in B / original stays, Alt-move removes from A and lands in B, no-op on the source tab. The real OS drag gesture (native drag image / Option cursor) + the "+"-button folder-picker flow remain manual-test-plan items.

**Status:** Shipped 2026-06-05. Cross-refs: §3 (copy/cut/paste tickets), §4.2 (always-tabbed strip + "+" button), §5 (attachments — the carry-over gap).

---

## 77. Paste files / images as attachments (`77-paste-attachments.md`)

HS-8662 (shipped 2026-06-05). A document-level `paste` listener (`src/client/pasteAttachments.ts`, wired from `app.tsx::init` next to the file-drop listener) creates attachments from clipboard files/images. Target by selection (`state.selectedIds`): **1 selected** → that ticket; **0 selected** → a new `Attachment`/`Attachments` ticket (mirrors the dropped-image fallback in `resolveDropTicketId`); **2+ selected** → no-op + a toast ("Pasting attachments to multiple tickets at once isn't supported"). Uploads via the existing `uploadAttachment(ticketId, file)` (§5), reloads the list, confirms with a toast.

**Focus rule.** A *file* paste is hijacked regardless of which plain text input/textarea has focus (a text field can't accept a file), so a screenshot pasted while the draft/title/search field is focused still attaches. A *text-only* paste carries no files → the handler returns early and the native paste runs (the internal ticket clipboard's keydown-driven Cmd/Ctrl+V, §3, is untouched). Only rich `contenteditable` surfaces are left fully alone. `extractClipboardFiles` prefers `clipboardData.files`, falls back to file-kind `clipboardData.items`.

**Tests.** Unit `pasteAttachments.test.ts` (target resolution by selection count + `extractClipboardFiles`); E2E `e2e/paste-attachment.spec.ts` (0→new ticket+file, 1→that ticket, 2+→toast no-op). **HS-8742 (shipped 2026-06-05) — new-ticket discoverability:** the 0-selected path now auto-selects + opens the created "Attachment(s)" ticket's detail panel (`selectAndOpenDetail` in `detail.tsx`); the drag-drop new-ticket fallback (`resolveDropTicketId`, now returning `{ id, createdNew }`) does the same after upload (§77.4).

**Status:** Shipped 2026-06-05. Cross-refs: §5 (attachments / upload path), §3 (internal ticket clipboard — distinct from OS file paste).

---

## 78. Announcer — A/V narration of project work (`78-announcer.md`)

**Status: Phase 1 after-the-fact core + live mode (§80) + tier-1/2 PIP visuals SHIPPED (HS-8745–8772, 2026-06-05); remaining: charts/screenshots (tier 3), Google Cloud TTS + cached audio (Phase 3), share-the-reel (Phase 4).** HS-7294 investigation. Opt-in, per-project audio/visual narrator of the work being done on a project — an "I stepped away while Claude worked" digest plus optional live narration. The doc thinks through value (strong: after-the-fact digest, PM-facing narrative, accessibility, marketing reel via §17; weak/gimmicky: narrating routine dev work, generated screenshots/diagrams), how the AI generates material (**derived** from existing signals — completion notes/`tickets.notes`, §14 command log, §67 telemetry, daily stats — via a decoupled summarization pass, plus an optional curated `hotsheet_announce` MCP tool), modes (after-the-fact + **live**, the latter elevated to a co-headline feature with a full detailed design in §78.4.1 — a producer/consumer queue accepting that *narration is slower than the work*, so near-live with a managed backlog: server-side generator on the long-poll `change-version`, collect→order→dedup signals, **debounce + coalesce** bursts into coherent entries, adaptive backlog compression, catch-up + skip-catch-up, a "still working" presence line from the §12 busy state, derived-vs-pushed latency trade-off, and cost/rate budgeting), playback controls, the draggable/resizable PIP (240×180 ↔ 960×720, modeled on §47 permission popup + §49 reader overlay; content tiers text → code-diffs → charts), TTS (default Web Speech API with a **WKWebView/Tauri-no-op caveat** to verify + Tauri-command/cloud fallback; optional Google Cloud TTS), and secrets (reuse `src/keychain.ts` §20 + the glassbox env→keychain→config 3-tier pattern). Phasing (live mode elevated to Phase 2 per the user — co-headline, not deferred): **Phase 0** spike (**HS-8744 done — GO**: ship `tts_speak` Tauri command over macOS `say` as the desktop primary so the WKWebView `speechSynthesis` risk is non-blocking; derived summaries sufficient for MVP; live-trigger latency ~20–300 ms — near-instant; identified Phase-1/2 wiring: per-project re-query off the global change-version, command-log events not on the fast signal, and missing `created_at >= since` query helpers), **Phase 1** after-the-fact audio-only core (the shared pipeline) + transcript PIP + keychain AI key, **Phase 2** live mode (§78.4.1 generator/consumer loop + catch-up + learn-from-skips + cost budget), **Phase 3** A/V + code-diff visuals + Google Cloud TTS, **Phase 4** rich generated visuals + share-the-reel. Data-model sketch: an `announcements` per-project table + per-project settings (`announcer_enabled`, `announcer_last_listened_at`, provider config, dismissed-topics). Open risks: WKWebView TTS reliability, cost/disclosure (work leaves the machine — privacy opt-in vs. §1.3 local-only), live-mode latency/ordering, visual-generation quality. **Phase 1a SHIPPED (HS-8745):** the server generation backbone, verified end-to-end with a real Anthropic key (derived summaries are good — a real run turned this session's completion notes into clean spoken entries in ~7 s). New `@anthropic-ai/sdk` dep; `announcements` table; `getLogEntries({ since })` filter; `src/announcer/{collectSignals,summarize,key}.ts`; `src/db/announcer.ts`; typed `src/api/announcer.ts`; `src/routes/announcer.ts` (`/api/announcer/{status,generate,entries,cursor,enabled,key,dismiss/:id,clear}`); settings `announcer_enabled` + `announcer_last_listened_at`; key in the keychain (§20). 27 unit/route tests. **Phase 1b SHIPPED (HS-8747):** the after-the-fact audio client. `src/client/tts.ts` (one `SpeechEngine`, two backends: Tauri `tts_speak`/`tts_stop` Rust commands over the OS voice [`say`/`spd-say`/PowerShell] = desktop primary, browser `speechSynthesis` = fallback; `speak()` returns `ended`/`cancelled`/`error`); `src/client/announcerPlayer.ts` (DOM-free playback state machine — play/pause/prev/next/skip, stale-resolution guard); `src/client/announcerPip.tsx` (non-modal corner-docked transcript PIP, z-index 2200 below reader/feedback/permission); `src/client/announcer.tsx` (header Listen button, gated on opted-in + has-key; generate→play→advance-cursor) + `src/client/announcerSettings.tsx` (Settings → Experimental section: enable toggle + write-only keychain key field + privacy disclosure). New Tauri commands `tts_speak` / `tts_stop` in `src-tauri/src/lib.rs`. 20 unit tests + `e2e/announcer.spec.ts`. Real audio + the Tauri voice path need a desktop/manual pass (can't verify headlessly). **Deferred to follow-ups:** 10s audio-timeline seeks (need cached audio — Phase 3 cloud TTS), text-emphasis markup, draggable/resizable PIP, "mark uninteresting" learning. Follow-up tickets track the phased build (live mode = Phase 2). **HS-8752 (bug, 2026-06-05):** a long-history project produced ~1.67M input tokens on a from-scratch generate and the Anthropic API rejected it (`prompt is too long > 1,000,000`); `collectSignals.capMaterial` now bounds the assembled material to `MAX_INPUT_TOKENS = 600_000`, keeping the most recent signals behind an elision marker. **HS-8751 (2026-06-05):** the announcer's key field moved to the global registry (§79) — it now *selects* an Anthropic key by name (`announcer_ai_key_id` setting), defaulting to the first; `POST /api/announcer/key-selection` replaced the raw-key `PUT /api/announcer/key`. **Phase 1b polish (2026-06-05):** **HS-8755** tightened the summarize prompt for concise (≤30-word) scripts; **HS-8753** added immediate busy feedback (toast + `.is-busy` spinner) on Listen; **HS-8756** the PIP now opens anchored under the Listen button, is draggable, and remembers its position (localStorage; pure geometry in `announcerPipPosition.ts`); **HS-8757** a minimize button hides the PIP back into the (now glowing) Listen button while playback continues, and a second click restores it; **HS-8754** a global `announcerSpeechRate` (0.5×–2×) speed control, adjustable from both the PIP and Settings → Experimental, plumbed through `SpeechEngine.speak(text, rate)` (browser `utterance.rate` / Tauri `say -r` WPM); **HS-8764** a global `announcerModel` setting (Settings → Experimental dropdown) defaulting to the **cheapest** model (Haiku 4.5) rather than Opus — registry in `src/announcer/models.ts` (cheapest-first), forwarded from the generate route to `summarizeWork`. **Cross-project (HS-8762 + HS-8758, 2026-06-05):** the announcer went cross-project. `GET /api/announcer/overview` enumerates every enabled project (each read in its own DB context via `runWithDataDir`) + the active secret; the PIP has a **context dropdown** ("All Projects" interleaves each enabled project's already-generated entries chronologically with per-entry project chips — no fresh generation; a specific project generates+plays its own reel). Default context = active project from a tab, "All Projects" from a global surface (dashboard/stats). The Listen button shows whenever *any* project is enabled+keyed (on all tabs), and the PIP is a persistent singleton that survives project switches (`reloadAppState` no longer tears it down). Typed callers take an optional `secret` (→ `apiWithSecret`) to target a non-active project; `AnnouncerPlayer<T>` is generic so entries carry their owning project for the chip + dismiss. Tests: overview route test, caller secret-targeting + overview tests, player `setEntries` test, `e2e/announcer.spec.ts` "All Projects" interleaving + chips. **Token + cost tracking (HS-8766, 2026-06-05):** each generate records the Anthropic `usage` (input/output tokens) + a per-model derived cost (`ANNOUNCER_PRICING`/`announcerCost` in `src/announcer/models.ts`) into a new `announcer_usage` table in the **shared telemetry DB** (`getTelemetryDb`, keyed by `project_secret`); `src/db/announcerUsage.ts` owns CRUD + rollups; surfaced as an "Announcer" card on the §71 per-project analytics dashboard and an "Announcer spend" section on the §70 cross-project page (new optional `announcer` fields on `getProjectRollupPayload`/`getDashboardPayload` + `src/api/telemetry.ts`). Always real $$ — the user's own Anthropic key — so it ignores the `telemetryCostMode` api/subscription toggle. Tests: pricing math, `announcerUsage` DB CRUD/rollups/scoping, route persists-usage. **Live mode Phase 2a (HS-8750, 2026-06-05 — server generator, §80):** `POST /api/announcer/live` registers a per-project live **lease** (`liveGenerator.ts`); while ≥1 project is live, a loop watches the global change-version, coalesces bursts (`coalescingTrigger.ts`, quiet 5 s / max-wait 25 s), and runs the shared `generate.ts::generateAnnouncementsOnce` per live project. **Off unless listening** — the 90 s client-renewed lease gates generation so it can't silently spend the key. `addLogEntry` now calls `notifyChange()` so command-log events ride the fast signal (wiring caveat b). Consumer/catch-up/presence = HS-8767 (2b); adaptive compression / mark-uninteresting-learning / cost budget / hybrid MCP tool = HS-8768–8771. See docs/80. **PIP enrichment (HS-8749, 2026-06-05, §78.5):** the two tractable enrichment items shipped — a **resizable PIP** (header expand toggle → `.announcer-pip.is-expanded` wider panel + taller body, remembered in `localStorage` and re-clamped on toggle) and **tier-1 text emphasis** (`summarizeWork` returns an optional `emphasis` array per entry — verbatim substrings of `script` — persisted in a new `announcements.emphasis` JSON column [`EmphasisArraySchema`], rendered by `src/client/announcerEmphasis.tsx` as `<strong class="announcer-em">` gradient with a plain-text fallback). Tests: emphasis range/render unit, DB round-trip, summarize-parses-emphasis, e2e emphasis + expand toggle. **Code-diff visuals SHIPPED (HS-8772, 2026-06-05, §78.5 tier 2):** a new `announcements.visuals` JSON column (`VisualsArraySchema`/`Visual` in `src/schemas.ts` — a discriminated union, only `{type:'diff', oldStr, newStr, filePath?, replaceAll?}` today; decoded in `src/db/announcer.ts`); the curated `hotsheet_announce` MCP tool gained an optional `diff` (`{oldStr, newStr, filePath?}`) so the working agent — which knows exactly what it changed — supplies the before/after (`CHANNEL_VERSION`/`EXPECTED_CHANNEL_VERSION` → 11), mapped to a `visuals` entry in `POST /api/announcer/announce`; the PIP renders it in a `.announcer-pip-visual` pane by **reusing the §47 permission diff renderer** (`src/client/editDiffPreview.tsx::renderEditDiffPreview`), shown only when the current entry carries a diff. The derived summarizer path produces no diffs (an AI summary of N signals can't be cleanly attributed to one commit-level diff). Tests: schema/DB round-trip, route maps diff→visual + no-diff→[], channel-tool forwards/validates diff, e2e diff pane renders + hides. **All Projects spoken project name (HS-8782, 2026-06-06):** in "All Projects" mode the narration now leads each entry with the owning project ("In <project>: <script>") since the visual chip isn't audible — pure `reelSpeechText` helper fed to a new `AnnouncerPlayer.speechTextFor` hook; single-project context unchanged. **Spoken permission checks (HS-8781, 2026-06-06):** a global default-on Announcer-tab toggle `announcerSpeakPermissions` reads each new permission popup aloud ("Permission needed: …") via the TTS voice — no API key/cost, works with no PIP open. `permissionOverlay.tsx::showPermissionPopupBody` → `announcePermission` (`announcerPermissionSpeech.ts`), cached pref in `announcerPermissionPref.ts`. Arbitration: never interrupts the in-flight narration segment — waits for the boundary (`AnnouncerPlayer.runAtNextBoundary`) and pre-empts upcoming segments; skips a permission already resolved (responded/dismissed) by speak time; deduped per `request_id`; long descriptions word-boundary-trimmed. Tests: `announcerPermissionSpeech.test.ts`, `announcerSpeechText.test.ts`, player boundary/`speechTextFor` cases. **Multi-provider + Apple Foundation Models (HS-8790, 2026-06-06):** the model registry is provider-tagged (`providerForModel`: `anthropic` | `apple`) and `summarizeWork` routes by provider — `apple` summarizes **on-device** (macOS 26 + Apple Intelligence, free/private, no key, `usage=null`) via a bundled Swift CLI helper the **server** shells out to (`src/announcer/appleFoundation.ts` → `src-tauri/apple-fm-helper/main.swift`; `--probe`/`--summarize` using FoundationModels **guided generation** for guaranteed structure, resolved via `HOTSHEET_APPLE_FM_BIN` or a `<cwd>/apple-fm-helper` fallback), so it works in Listen AND live mode. The helper is **verified compiling + running on macOS 26.5 / Xcode 26.5**; `npm run build:apple-fm-helper` builds it (auto-run by `npm run tauri:dev`, which the dev server then discovers via cwd — no env/bundling needed for dev). Availability (`appleAvailable` on `/status`+`/overview`) makes Apple the **default when present** (explicit `announcerModel` wins) and drops the API-key requirement; the settings UI is reordered **model-first** with the Anthropic-key field shown only for Anthropic models. Native compile/sign/run is a desktop task (`scripts/build-apple-fm-helper.sh`, guarded; see docs/tauri-architecture.md). Tests: provider routing in `models.test`/`summarize.test`, `appleFoundation.test` (availability matrix + subprocess contract). Cross-platform **local/Ollama** provider SHIPPED (HS-8792, see §81). **Spoken-permission project name (HS-8794, 2026-06-06):** the spoken permission check now names the owning project ("Permission needed in <project>: …", resolved from the popup secret via `projectsByIdSignal`; un-prefixed fallback when unknown) — `announcePermission(perm, projectName)`. **Channel chatter out of the reel (HS-8795, 2026-06-06):** `collectWorkSignals` drops `permission_request` (needed + granted) and `done` ("Claude finished") command-log events from the narrated material (the live spoken announcement already covers permissions; resolved grants / "Claude finished" are noise); `trigger` events stay. **Mid-task ("more live") narration off the §67 telemetry event stream SHIPPED (HS-8789, see §82).** **Dynamic Anthropic model discovery + same-family upgrade (HS-8853, 2026-06-17):** the Anthropic options in the model dropdown are no longer hardcoded — `src/announcer/anthropicModels.ts` queries the Models API (`client.models.list()`, filtered to `claude-*`, 5-min per-key TTL cache) so the list tracks what the user's key offers (new models appear, retired drop off); `/api/announcer/status` returns `anthropicModels`, falling back to the static `ANNOUNCER_MODELS` set when there's no key/discovery fails. The Models API has **no pricing** (no pricing endpoint), so `announcerCost` keeps a maintained map but falls back by **family** (haiku/sonnet/opus) for an unlisted id. A saved model the key no longer offers upgrades to the **newest same-family** model (`resolveBestModelForSelection`: retired `claude-sonnet-4-5` → `claude-sonnet-4-6`, never a jump to opus), applied by `resolveAnnouncerModel` at generate time and mirrored in the settings dropdown; `announcerModel` now accepts any `claude-*` id (not a fixed enum). Also fixed the v0.20.0-beta.1 e2e failure — every PIP test tripped the HS-8435 strict-error gate on an unmocked `/announcer/listened` 403 (now mocked in a shared `beforeEach`). Tests: `anthropicModels.test.ts`, `models.test.ts`, `generate.test.ts`, `e2e/announcer.spec.ts`. **Opt-in Apple fallback model (HS-8891, 2026-06-19):** the HS-8805 auto-fallback deliberately skips an *explicit* Apple choice; HS-8891 adds an opt-in `announcerFallbackModel` (global config; non-apple — a `claude-*` id or `local`, `''`=none) used when an explicit **Apple** primary fails inference (the HS-8883 "code 4" class). Pure policy `generate.ts::decideAnnouncerFallback`; `summarizeWork`'s `fallbackModel` opt routes the failure to Anthropic (via the key) or local (via the endpoint). Settings shows a "Fallback model if Apple Intelligence fails" dropdown only for an Apple primary (None + Anthropic models + local-when-available). Scope (ticket decisions): Apple-primary only, Anthropic-or-local fallback, applies to both Live + manual. Tests: `summarize.test.ts`, `generate.test.ts`, `e2e/announcer.spec.ts`. **Apple provider switched to the `apple-fm` package (HS-8907, 2026-06-20):** the hand-maintained Swift helper + build are gone — removed `src-tauri/apple-fm-helper/main.swift` and `scripts/build-apple-fm-helper.sh` (+ the `build:apple-fm-helper` npm script and the dedicated macOS-26 CI compile job). `src/announcer/appleFoundation.ts` is now a thin wrapper over the **`apple-fm`** npm package (a direct dependency): `isAppleFoundationAvailable()` → `probe().available` (cached); `runAppleFoundationSummarize(system, material, schema)` → `generate({system, prompt: material, schema})` with guided generation (the `OUTPUT_SCHEMA` is threaded in from `summarize.ts`). `apple-fm` ships a prebuilt signed+notarized `bin/apple-fm-helper`, resolved via `APPLE_FM_BIN` → bundled binary → PATH — so **dev needs no build step** (found in `node_modules`). Tauri packaging: `build-sidecar.sh` COPIES that binary into `server/apple-fm-helper`, the macOS pre-sign step re-signs it with our identity, and `lib.rs` sets `APPLE_FM_BIN` (was `HOTSHEET_APPLE_FM_BIN`). Tests rewritten to inject fake `probe`/`generate` (`appleFoundation.test.ts`); `summarize.test.ts` unchanged. **Desktop validation TODO:** a real signed/notarized arm64 `tauri:build` + on-device run hasn't been done in this environment. **Still deferred:** 10s audio-timeline seeks (blocked on Phase 3 cached audio `announcements.audio_path`).

## 79. Global API-Key Registry (`79-api-keys.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8751, 2026-06-05; UI revised HS-8759/8760/8761/8763).** A machine-global list of named API keys that every project selects from by name, instead of re-entering a secret per project. Each key = **type** (fixed enum, **`anthropic_api_key` only** — HS-8763 dropped `google_tts_key` until Google Cloud TTS ships) + **name** (free text) + **value** (write-only secret) + **created_at/updated_at** (HS-8760). **Storage is split** so secrets never hit config/git: metadata `{ id, type, name, created_at, updated_at }` → `~/.hotsheet/config.json` (`keys`, `SecretKeyMetaSchema`); value → OS keychain (plugin id `keys`, account = id). **Per-project selection** stores a key id (announcer: `announcer_ai_key_id`) and **defaults to the first key of the matching type** when unset (`resolveKeyValueByType`). New: `src/secret-keys.ts` (store), `src/routes/keys.ts` + `src/api/keys.ts` (`GET/POST /api/keys`, `PUT/DELETE /api/keys/:id`), `src/client/keysSettings.tsx` (Settings → "API Keys" tab; broadcasts `hotsheet:keys-changed` so the announcer selector refreshes live), `src/client/timeAgo.ts` (shared "N ago" formatter). **UI (HS-8759/8760/8761):** each row has a static type label (type immutable post-create), an edit-value dialog button, a lucide trash delete, and a "Created …/Updated …" provenance label; "Add a key…" opens a dialog with full-width Name + Value (in-app overlays via `openKeyFormDialog`, never `window.prompt`). The announcer settings replaced its key input with an Anthropic-key dropdown. Tests: `secret-keys.test.ts` / `api/keys.test.ts` / `routes/keys.test.ts` / `announcer/key.test.ts` + `e2e/keys.spec.ts`; real-keychain persistence is a manual item. **Scope:** Anthropic AI keys only — folding plugin secrets (§20) into the registry is deferred.

## 80. Announcer Live Mode (`80-announcer-live-mode.md`)

**Status: Phase 2a (server generator) + 2b (client consumer) SHIPPED (HS-8750 + HS-8767, 2026-06-05); richer policies pending.** The producer half of the §78.4.1 live-mode design — near-live narration of work as it happens. While ≥1 client holds a per-project live **lease** (`POST /api/announcer/live`, TTL 90 s, client-renewed), `src/announcer/liveGenerator.ts` watches the global change-version (`addPollWaiter`), coalesces bursts into one batch (`src/announcer/coalescingTrigger.ts` — quiet 5 s / max-wait 25 s, pure + clock-injectable), and runs the shared `src/announcer/generate.ts::generateAnnouncementsOnce` per live project in its own DB context (collect → summarize → persist `announcements` → record usage HS-8766). **Off unless listening** — the lease gates generation so it can never silently spend the user's key; expired leases stop the loop. Wiring caveat (b): `addLogEntry` now `notifyChange()`s so command-log events ride the fast signal. The generate core is shared with the manual `POST /api/announcer/generate` route. **2b consumer SHIPPED (HS-8767):** `src/client/announcerLive.ts` (`LiveSession`) renews the lease + tails new entries (3 s poll, `projectSecret:id` dedup), pausing while the window is hidden; `AnnouncerPlayer` gained `appendEntries` + `jumpToLast` (skip-catch-up); the PIP added a Live toggle + "● working…/✓ idle" presence line (from §12 `getProjectBusySecrets`) + skip-to-live. **Generator refinements SHIPPED:** **HS-8768** adaptive backlog compression (≥6 unplayed entries → `buildSystemPrompt({compression:'high'})` produces 1–2 maximally-merged entries; `backlogCompressionLevel` threshold) + **HS-8769** learn-from-skips (skipping records the entry title in per-project `announcer_dismissed_topics`, injected into the prompt as an omit-list; editable via `GET/PUT /api/announcer/dismissed-topics` + a Settings textarea; `src/announcer/dismissedTopics.ts`). **HS-8770 cost/rate budget + disclosure SHIPPED** (`src/announcer/callBudget.ts` — 6 summarize calls/60 s per project via `tryConsumeCall`, gated as `canSummarize` in `generateAnnouncementsOnce`; over budget → skip + defer; one-time spend/privacy `confirmDialog` on first Live-enable). **HS-8771 hybrid MCP tool SHIPPED:** a 15th `hotsheet_*` tool `hotsheet_announce({title, highlight})` (`src/channel.tools.ts`, `CHANNEL_VERSION`/`EXPECTED_CHANNEL_VERSION` → 10) → `POST /api/announcer/announce` inserts a curated `announcements` row directly (no AI call; no-op when the announcer's off) for the live consumer to tail. **Live mode is now complete end-to-end (2a + 2b + all four refinements).** Tests: `coalescingTrigger.test.ts`, `liveGenerator.test.ts`, `routes/announcer.test.ts` (`/live` gate).

---

## 93. WebSocket Push Synchronization (`93-websocket-push-sync.md`)

**Status: Design only (HS-7945, 2026-06-24) — decomposed into schedulable sub-tickets, awaiting scheduling.** Implementation design for the `/ws/sync` WebSocket channel that replaces the `/api/poll` long-poll for multi-client deployments — the transport layer of the §46 remote epic. **Grounding:** today's `/api/poll` is already a long-poll (server holds up to 30s, flushes instantly on `notifyMutation` via `src/routes/notify.ts`), so on the single-local default updates are already effectively instant; the WebSocket win is **bandwidth at N clients / over a remote link** (push the delta, not a full re-`GET`). **Additive** — `/api/poll` stays as the automatic fallback, so the single-machine user never regresses. **Design:** a pure server **event bus** (`src/sync/eventBus.ts` — monotonic `seq`, bounded per-project ring [default 1000], sink registry, typed zod event union in `src/schemas.ts`); a `/ws/sync` endpoint reusing the existing `ws`-`noServer`-mode transport already shipped for terminal PTYs (`src/terminals/websocket.ts`) with secret + HS-7940 trusted-origin auth, `?since=<seq>` catch-up / `resync` on eviction, and a 20s ping/pong heartbeat; mutation routes emit `emitEvent` after the HTTP response (alongside the retained counter bump); a client reducer (`src/client/wsSync.ts`) with per-event store mutation, exponential-backoff reconnect (1→30s), and auto-fallback to `/api/poll` + a "live updates unavailable" hint on double-drop. **Decomposition (HS-8978 bus → HS-8979 endpoint [blocked by HS-7940] → HS-8980 emission → HS-8981 client+e2e → HS-8982 backpressure/coalescing v2);** `blocked_by` gates encode the ordering. Out of scope (tracked elsewhere): conflict UX + `If-Match` + plugin-sync audit (HS-7946/§46.4), per-client filtering, cross-project subscription. Downstream consumer: HS-8973 (live-push the claimed-by chip off this bus instead of its 5s poll).

---

## 92. Coordinator-Dispatch UX (`92-coordinator-dispatch.md`)

**Status: SHIPPED 2026-06-24 (HS-8964 + HS-8974 + HS-8965).** Drag-a-ticket-onto-a-worker-tile + a "Dispatch to worker…" context menu (`src/client/dispatch.ts` → claim-by-id, 409 → "already claimed by X"); `claimNext` serves each worker its own-claimed (dispatched) tickets first as a personal queue (regardless of `up_next`), so the self-claim loop drains them with no worker change. **Reassign/recall (§92.7 → HS-8974):** re-dispatching a claimed ticket prompts → force claim-by-id (`ClaimSchema.force`, atomic overwrite) moves it; a "Recall claim" context-menu item force-releases back to the pool. **AI partition-into-N-chunks (§92.6 → HS-8965):** `src/workers/partition.ts` + the shared `announcerJson.ts` provider call + `POST /api/workers/partition` + an "AI: partition" panel button (review-in-confirm → dispatch each chunk; round-robin fallback). **Queue-only mode (§92.9 → HS-8975):** a per-tile toggle (`claimNext({ownOnly})` + `poolManager.queueOnly` + `POST /workers/pool/queue-only`) makes a worker work only its dispatched tickets then stop, instead of self-claiming the shared pool (default off = fall back). Only an in-dialog editable partition (HS-8977) is a follow-up. The "push" half of §90.5's dual coordination — owner manually assigns related Up Next tickets onto a specific worker so a coherent change set lands in one worktree (complements autonomous self-claim). **Interaction:** mirrors §76 cross-project drag — drag selected ticket rows/cards (existing `setDraggedTicketIds`) onto a **worker tile** in the pool panel (§91), `dropEffect=move`, §76 single-slot `.drag-over` highlight; plus a Tauri-safe "Dispatch to worker ▸" context-menu fallback. **Server:** claim-by-id (`POST /api/tickets/:id/claim`, HS-8862) where the claimer is the *target worker* — sets `claimed_by`=that worker + lease; 409 if already live-leased. **Coexistence:** the dispatched ticket's live lease makes other workers' `claim-next` skip it — no special-casing; mixed dispatch+self-claim is the default. **Shows** via the claimed-by chip (§90.8/HS-8864) + the worker tile's queue. **Optional AI "partition into N coherent chunks"** helper (reuses §91.6 relatedness analysis → assignments; owner reviews before apply). Edge cases: dispatch-blocked (queued + warned), dispatch-to-draining (rejected), reassign/recall by re-drag. Gated on HS-8862 + HS-8960 (panel) + HS-8864. Tauri-drag caveat → E2E uses the menu path.

## 91. Worker-Pool Dynamic Scaling + AI-Suggested N (`91-worker-pool-scaling.md`)

**Status: Partial — the pool manager + minimal panel SHIPPED 2026-06-23 (HS-8962).** Implemented: `src/workers/poolManager.ts` (in-memory, session-only, per-`dataDir` slot registry + drain flag), **drain-aware `claim-next`** (the route calls `onClaimNext` → a draining pool worker gets `{ticket:null, drain:true}` + is flipped to `stopped`, finishing its current ticket first; the `hotsheet-worker` skill honors it, `SKILL_VERSION`→12), `GET /api/workers/pool` + `POST /api/workers/pool/{register,drain,drain-all,remove,target}` (typed in `src/api/workers.ts`), and the worker-pool panel `src/client/workerPoolPanel.tsx` (git popover → "Worker pool…": tile per worker w/ state + current ticket, "+ Add worker", per-worker Drain, Drain all; auto-cleans stopped workers; polls 3 s). Tests: `workers/poolManager.test.ts`, `api/workers.test.ts`, `routes/api.test.ts` (pool block + drain-aware claim-next), `client/workerPoolPanel.test.ts`. **Also SHIPPED — numeric target-N stepper + reconcile (HS-8971):** the panel's `− N +` stepper sets the server `targetN` (`setPoolTarget`), and `reconcile()` (each refresh) adds workers when the live count is below / gracefully drains the idle-first surplus when above (a failed launch lowers the target so it doesn't retry forever). **Also SHIPPED — zombie-slot reap (HS-8972, §91.7):** each slot tracks `lastSeenAt` (bumped on claim-next / renew / claim via `poolManager.touch`); a slot silent past `STALE_AFTER_MS` (5 min) derives state `dead`, which the panel auto-reaps (terminal + worktree + unregister) + the reconcile recreates to target N. **Also SHIPPED — AI-suggested N (HS-8963, §91.6):** `src/workers/suggestN.ts` + `GET /api/workers/suggest-n` + an "AI: suggest" panel button — the configured announcer provider (Anthropic / local / Apple — `runEstimator` routes via `resolveAnnouncerModel`+`providerForModel`, mirroring `summarize.ts`; HS-8976) estimates independent-parallel clusters over the unblocked Up Next digest → `{n, rationale}` clamped to `[1, poolMax()]`; deterministic cluster heuristic when no provider can run. Still design-only: the live event bus (HS-7945; polling for now). (Dispatch drop targets shipped in HS-8964; the claimed-by chip in HS-8864.) Original design follows. Runtime management over §90.7's durable worktree worker pool. A **worker slot** = one git worktree (HS-8935) + a per-worktree AI terminal (HS-8936) running the §90.5.1/HS-8863 claim loop, with a stable `worker_label` and states starting→idle⇄working→draining→stopped. **Scale up:** automate §89 Phase B/C — createWorktree on a fresh per-worker branch (follower pointer → owner) + open the claim-loop terminal; incremental, non-blocking. **Scale down (graceful):** mark `draining` → loop stops claiming → finishes current ticket → release → close terminal + removeWorktree (branch kept per §89.5); **never kill mid-ticket** (force-stop relies on lease expiry to reclaim). **Worker-pool panel:** extends the worktrees panel (HS-8938) into a dashboard — per-worker tiles (label, state, current ticket + lease freshness via HS-8864), target-N stepper / add / drain-one / drain-all, AI-suggest-N button; also hosts the §92 dispatch drop targets. **AI-suggested N:** a recommendation (owner sets actual N) — analyzes the Up Next set + flat `blocked_by` graph (HS-8865) to estimate independent-parallel clusters, `N=clamp(clusters,1,POOL_MAX)` + a one-line rationale, run via the AI plumbing not a hand-rolled estimator. Edge cases: empty-pool idle-backoff, crash→lease reclaim, single-local default untouched (N=0 ⇒ today's flow), single-machine scope. Gated on HS-8862 + HS-8863.

## 90. Distributed Ticket Execution — claim/lease + worker pool (`90-distributed-execution.md`)

**Status: Partial — the claim/lease primitive (HS-8862), the flat `blocked_by` gate (HS-8865), AND the single-worker loop + launcher (HS-8863) SHIPPED 2026-06-23.** §90.2-90.4 implemented: the four orthogonal `tickets` columns (`claimed_by`/`claim_lease_expires_at`/`worker_label`/`claim_count`), `src/db/claims.ts` (atomic `claimNext` via SKIP LOCKED ordered by the worklist PRIORITY_ORD, `claimById` w/ 409 on live foreign lease, `renewLease`, `release`, `getClaims`, `sweepExpiredClaims`), the five endpoints (`POST /tickets/claim-next` `/:id/claim` `/:id/renew-lease` `/:id/release` + `GET /tickets/claims`, typed in `src/api/tickets.ts`), the 3 MCP tools (`hotsheet_claim_next`/`renew_lease`/`release`, CHANNEL_VERSION→12, 18 tools), and a 60s lease-sweep timer (`src/claims/leaseSweepTimer.ts`, wired in cli.ts/lifecycle.ts). Tests: `db/claims.test.ts` (9) + `routes/api.test.ts` claim block (4) + `channel.tools.test.ts` (+4) + `claims/leaseSweepTimer.test.ts` (4). **Also SHIPPED — flat blocked_by gate (HS-8865):** `ticket_blocked_by` join table + `src/db/blockedBy.ts` (`setBlockedBy` with self/unknown/cycle rejection, `getBlockedBy`/`isBlocked`/`getBlockedByMap`, `BLOCKED_TICKET_IDS_SQL`); `claimNext` excludes blocked tickets; `GET`/`PUT /tickets/:id/blocked-by` + `hotsheet_set_blocked_by` MCP tool (CHANNEL_VERSION→13, 19 tools); a blocked ticket becomes claimable once every blocker is completed/verified. Tests: `db/blockedBy.test.ts` + route + tool suites. **Also SHIPPED — single-worker loop + launcher (HS-8863):** `src/workers/workerLoop.ts` (`startWorker` → `{stop,done}`) is the canonical claim→work→complete+release→repeat loop (lease heartbeat, graceful stop only between tickets, skip-completion on lost lease, park-on-error so a poison ticket can't hot-loop); `src/workers/launchWorker.ts` (`prepareWorker` + `workerLaunchCommand` → `claude "/hotsheet-worker"`) ensures a follower worktree slot + `POST /api/workers/launch` (typed `launchWorker`); the interactive production worker is the Claude-only `hotsheet-worker` skill (`SKILL_VERSION`→11). Tests: `workers/workerLoop.test.ts` (incl. two-worker no-double-claim + dead-worker reclaim), `workers/launchWorker.test.ts`, `api/workers.test.ts`, `skills.test.ts`. **Also SHIPPED — poison-ticket dead-letter (HS-8970):** `claimNext` only offers a ticket while `claim_count < MAX_CLAIM_ATTEMPTS` (=5), and `sweepExpiredClaims` quarantines an over-budget reclaimed ticket (`up_next=false` + `needs-attention` tag + `QUARANTINED:` note + resets `claim_count` so a re-star retries) — reusing up_next+tags, no new column. Tests in `db/claims.test.ts`. **Also SHIPPED — claimed-by chip + in-flight view (HS-8864):** the reactive `src/client/claimsStore.ts` (5 s poll + 1 s countdown tick off `GET /api/tickets/claims`) feeds a `⚙ <worker> · m:ss` chip (live + pulsing-stale states, `src/client/claimedByChip.tsx`) on ticket rows + the detail header, plus an "In-flight work…" overlay (`src/client/inflightPanel.tsx`, git popover) listing every claimed ticket. Poll-based until the HS-7945 bus; HS-7946 clientId labels still design (uses `worker_label`). Tests: `claimedByChip`/`claimsStore`/`inflightPanel`. **Also SHIPPED — coordinator-dispatch (HS-8964):** drag-a-ticket-onto-a-worker-tile + a "Dispatch to worker…" context menu (`src/client/dispatch.ts` → claim-by-id), with `claimNext` serving each worker its own-claimed (dispatched) tickets first as a personal queue (no worker-loop change). The single-machine §90/§91/§92 epic is complete (incl. the AI suggest-N + partition helpers); only the §46 remote epic + minor follow-ups (HS-8973 chip-push, HS-8977 editable partition) remain. Pins the claim/lease model that worktree Phase D (§89) consumes — written first per HS-8937 feedback (1b). **Claim/lease schema:** four orthogonal nullable `tickets` columns (`claimed_by`, `claim_lease_expires_at`, `worker_label`, `claim_count`) via the idempotent `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` block; unused ⇒ behavior identical to today (single-local default unaffected). **Lease:** ~120 s TTL (Announcer live-mode pattern), worker heartbeat `renew-lease`, dual expiry — lazy (claim treats expired as claimable) + active §75-scheduler sweep that clears `claimed_by` + appends a "lease expired — reclaimed" note; reclaim leaves `status` untouched. **Atomic claim-next:** `SELECT … FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` ordered by the SAME `PRIORITY_ORD` the Up Next worklist uses, excluding blocked tickets. **Endpoints:** `POST /tickets/claim-next` / `:id/claim` (409 on live foreign lease) / `:id/renew-lease` / `:id/release` + `GET /tickets/claims` (typed in `src/api/tickets.ts`). **MCP tools:** `hotsheet_claim_next`/`hotsheet_renew_lease`/`hotsheet_release` (bump CHANNEL_VERSION 11→12 both files). **Both coordination models (feedback 2):** self-claim (idle worker pulls) AND coordinator-dispatch (owner assigns related chunks via claim-by-id) — coexist via the live-lease skip. **Flat `blocked_by` gate (HS-8865):** `ticket_blocked_by` join table excludes blocked tickets from claim-next; flat only, never hierarchical. **Worker pool (feedback 3):** durable per-worker slots (N long-lived worktrees, not per-ticket ephemeral) with dynamic scale up/down (graceful drain after current ticket) + AI-suggested N. **Single-machine first (feedback 4):** N workers vs the local server; §46 remote epic only for off-box. Implementation tickets: HS-8862 (primitive ✅) / HS-8863 (worker loop ✅) / HS-8865 (gate ✅) / HS-8970 (dead-letter ✅) / HS-8962 (pool manager + panel ✅) / HS-8971 (target-N stepper ✅) / HS-8864 (claimed-by chip + in-flight view ✅) / HS-8964 (coordinator-dispatch ✅) / HS-8974 (reassign/recall ✅) / HS-8972 (zombie-slot recovery ✅) / HS-8963 (AI-suggested N ✅) / HS-8976 (suggest-N provider parity ✅) / HS-8965 (AI-partition ✅) / HS-8973 (chip live-push/labels, backlog) / HS-8975 (queue-only mode ✅) / HS-8977 (editable partition, backlog).

## 89. Git Worktrees + Per-Worktree AI Agents (`89-git-worktrees.md`)

**Status: Partial — design (HS-8905) + Phase A shipped (HS-8934), 2026-06-22.** Phase A = the follower `.hotsheet/settings.json` `authoritativeDataDir` pointer + `resolveAuthoritativeDataDir()` redirect (one validated hop; throws on self-ref/missing/chain), applied at the `cli.ts` + `registerProject`/`registerExistingProject` data-dir chokepoints so launching from a worktree shares the owner's one DB/instance. Tests: `file-settings.test.ts` + `worktreeFollower.e2e.test.ts`. **Phase B server core shipped (HS-8935):** `src/worktrees.ts` create/list/remove worktrees (`git worktree` shelled async via injectable runner; create writes the follower pointer → owner; symlink-robust path matching) + `GET/POST /api/worktrees` + `POST /api/worktrees/remove` (typed `src/api/worktrees.ts`). Tests: `worktrees.test.ts` (real-git create/list/remove/deleteBranch) + `api/worktrees.test.ts`. **Phase B UI shipped (HS-8938):** `src/client/worktreesPanel.tsx` overlay (list/create/remove worktrees) opened from a "Manage worktrees…" button in the git popover; remove via `confirmDialog`. **Phase C shipped (HS-8936):** per-worktree AI terminal — each panel row's "Open terminal" runs `claude` in the worktree cwd (`openTerminalRunningCommand` now takes `cwd`); agent wiring written at create time — `registerChannelAt(worktreeRoot, ownerDataDir)` (owner-direct `.mcp.json`, decision 2) + `ensureSkillsForDir(worktreeRoot, undefined, ownerDataDir)` (skills' worklist/port/secret → owner, decision 1a; `skills.ts` threads an optional `dataDir` override). Tests: `worktreesPanel.test.ts`, `channel-config.test.ts` (registerChannelAt), `skills.test.ts` (override), `worktrees.test.ts` (.mcp.json wiring). **Phase D designed (HS-8937, 2026-06-23)** — claim model resolved in §90 ([`90-distributed-execution.md`](../90-distributed-execution.md)); Phase D shape pinned: durable per-worker worktree pool, dynamic scale up/down + AI-suggested N, both coordination modes, single-machine first. Implementation gated (HS-8862/8863/8864/8865 + HS-8960/8961). Goal: run several git worktrees of one repo side by side, each with its own AI terminal, all talking to ONE Hot Sheet instance / ticket DB, eventually auto-parallelizing tickets across them. Worktrees = the "isolated checkout" substrate for the distributed-execution epic (HS-8863). **Shared-instance model (user's choice):** a worktree gets a lightweight follower `.hotsheet/settings.json` that points to an authoritative/owner `.hotsheet` folder; everything that resolves a project data-dir from the worktree (CLI/server, channel, MCP/skills, markdown, git chip) redirects to the owner, so a Claude terminal in a worktree drives the one shared DB (reuses single-instance + channel multi-connection). One validated hop (no chains/cycles); pointer is local/gitignored. Phases: A follower pointer + redirect resolver (keystone, single-machine), B worktree management (create/list/remove + write follower pointer/.mcp.json/skills), C per-worktree AI terminal (existing terminal system, worktree cwd, wired to authoritative instance), D auto-parallelization (gated on claim/lease HS-8862 + worker loop HS-8863). Prereqs: HS-8861–8865 (claim/lease "ticket checkout" + worker loop + UI + planning gate) and §46 remote epic (HS-7940 bind+auth / HS-7944 service-only / HS-7945 WebSocket bus) — §46 only needed for *remote* workers; single-machine multi-worktree works against the local server. Flat `blocked_by` only (no hierarchical sub-tasks). Follow-up tickets filed in backlog (Phase A–D).

## 88. Scheduled Periodic Plugin Sync (`88-scheduled-sync.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8933, 2026-06-22).** Background auto-sync for ticketing plugins, generic in the sync engine (`src/plugins/syncEngine.ts`), first adopter GitHub Issues. A plugin opts in via a `sync_interval_minutes` manifest preference; GitHub ships it as a select (Off/1/5/15/30/60, **default 15 = on**, min 1). Per-project setting (`plugin:<id>:sync_interval_minutes`). Timers keyed per `(plugin, dataDir)` (`${pluginId}::${dataDir}`) so projects schedule independently; `syncRunCounts` tracks each timer's run number. Each run is **incremental** except the **first run + ~hourly** which do a **full reconcile** (`runSync(id, { fullPull })`) to self-heal the HS-8931 stranding class; `fullEvery = max(1, round(60/intervalMin))`. Engine API: `startScheduledSync`/`stopScheduledSync(pluginId, dataDir?)`/`stopAllScheduledSyncs`/`isSyncScheduled`/`applyScheduledSyncFromConfig(pluginId, dataDir)` (reads the project setting + manifest default, honors per-project enablement, idempotent). Lifecycle: boot `scheduleSyncsForAllProjects()` after `loadAllPlugins()` (server-side, no client needed); `registerProject`/`registerExistingProject` call `scheduleSyncsForProject`; enable/disable/reactivate routes re-apply; `stopAllScheduledSyncs()` on shutdown. GitHub plugin manifest bumped 0.5.5 → 0.6.0 so the bundled-plugin auto-update propagates the new field. Tests: `syncEngine.test.ts` (first-run full pull self-heals a stranded issue; per-project keying; `applyScheduledSyncFromConfig` start/default/disabled/off/no-pref). **HS-8791 (out-of-sync badge, shipped 2026-06-22):** sync toolbar buttons show a count badge of how out of sync the project is in **both directions** (`total = toPull + toPush`, hidden at 0, `99+` cap). `getPendingSyncCounts(backend)` (read-only): toPull = remote changes vs the incremental watermark (one remote read; failure → 0), toPush = dirty tickets + outbox ops (write-capable only). Server `GET /plugins/:id/pending-count` (`ok:false` when disabled/unconfigured); client `src/client/pluginSyncBadge.tsx` polls **every 5 min while visible** for the active project + refreshes after sync/toolbar-render. Tests: `syncEngine.test.ts` getPendingSyncCounts cases + `pluginSyncBadge.test.ts` (6, happy-dom) + `api/plugins.test.ts` path.

## 87. Isolated Test Instance (`87-test-instance.md`)

**Status: Partial — foundation (HS-8920) + `--test` launcher (HS-8921) + TEST badge (HS-8922) shipped 2026-06-22; keychain namespacing (HS-8923) deferred.** Goal (parent investigation HS-8919): run a test copy of Hot Sheet that touches none of the real `~/.hotsheet` global state or real projects and can't collide with the prod instance. **HS-8920 (shipped)** introduces the one switch for relocating global state: new `globalHotsheetDir()` (`src/global-dir.ts`, single export) returns `process.env.HOTSHEET_HOME` (empty/whitespace treated as unset) else `join(homedir(), '.hotsheet')`. Every global resolver now routes through it — `global-config.ts` (`config.json`), `project-list.ts` (`projects.json`), `instance.ts` (`instance.json`), `startup-log.ts` (`startup.log`), `db/connection.ts` (`telemetry/`), `update-check.ts` (`last-update-check`), `plugins/loader.ts` (`plugins/`, `dismissed-plugins.json`, `plugin-config.json`), `routes/plugins.ts` (`plugins/`). The two pre-existing narrow overrides keep precedence over the new root: `HOTSHEET_STARTUP_LOG` and `HOTSHEET_TELEMETRY_DIR` (specific override → `HOTSHEET_HOME` → `homedir()/.hotsheet`). **HS-8921 (shipped) — `--test` flag** (`src/cli/args.ts`): turnkey isolated instance. Sets `HOTSHEET_HOME=~/.hotsheet-test` (stable, when unset), default port `4274` (`TEST_MODE_PORT`), sandbox data-dir `<HOTSHEET_HOME>/sandbox-project/.hotsheet` (so launching from inside a real project never writes `.hotsheet/` into it), and `setTestMode(true)` (new `src/test-mode.ts`, mirrors `demo-mode.ts`, read by the page shell for the badge). Each default applies only when the explicit flag wasn't passed (order-independent). `maybeApplyTestModeHome(argv)` runs at the very top of `cli.ts::main()` (before `initStartupLog`) so even the startup log lands in the test home; `--test --replace` can only target a prior test instance (isolated `instance.json`). Convenience: `npm run dev:test`; Tauri forwards `--test` to the sidecar (`collect_forwarded_server_args`). **HS-8922 (shipped) — TEST badge:** `routes/pages.tsx` renders a `.test-instance-badge` (amber `TEST :<port>` pill, port from the `Host` header) as the first `app-header` child when `isTestMode()`, styled in `styles.scss`; absent on a normal launch. **Not relocated (by design):** the OS keychain (`com.hotsheet.plugin.*` service names — deferred HS-8923) and `~/.claude/` (real Claude auth stays shared). Per-project `.hotsheet/` is selected by `--data-dir`/cwd, independent of `HOTSHEET_HOME`. Tests: `src/global-dir.test.ts` (8) + `src/global-dir.e2e.test.ts` (HOTSHEET_HOME relocation, spawned child); `src/cli/args.test.ts` (6 — `--test` defaults + explicit-flag precedence) + `src/test-mode.test.ts` + `src/cli.testMode.e2e.test.ts` (spawned `--test`: binds 4274, global state under `.hotsheet-test`, sandbox DB, cwd left clean, served page contains the TEST badge); Rust `dev_server_args_tests` (`--test` forwarding); badge: `src/routes/pages.test.tsx` (present + port / present without port / absent) + `e2e/test-badge.spec.ts` (absent in a real browser on normal launch).

## 86. AI Assistant Setup (`86-ai-assistant-setup.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8913, 2026-06-21) — Claude Code / CLAUDE.md only; Cursor/Windsurf/Copilot deferred to HS-8916.** Installs + keeps current Hot Sheet's three recommended AI-assistant instruction sections in a project's `CLAUDE.md`: **Ticket-Driven Work**, **Testing Philosophy**, **Requirements Documentation** (canonical text in `src/aiInstructions.ts::MANAGED_SECTIONS`; also published as copy-paste blocks in the README). Each section sits between **versioned HTML-comment markers** (`<!-- hotsheet:begin section=ID v=N -->` … `end`); `getInstructionsStatus`/`applyManagedSections` detect presence/version, rewrite the **prescribed** portion in place when behind the current version (idempotent), append absent sections, and never touch surrounding user content. The testing + requirements sections carry a **self-healing "this project's specifics" sub-block** — a `<!-- hotsheet:needs-setup -->` sentinel + an instruction telling the reading AI to detect/confirm the project's actual test runner, file globs, commands, and docs layout, then replace the block (removing the sentinel). Unfilled blocks may be refreshed; **filled blocks are preserved verbatim forever**; user-deleted blocks aren't re-added. Triggers: (1) once-per-project boot nudge (`src/client/aiInstructionsNudge.tsx`, `decideNudgeAction` — silent auto-update when sections already present but behind; prompt only when none present AND Claude detected AND not previously dismissed, dismissal persisted as `ai_instructions_nudge_dismissed` in `settings.json`); (2) Settings → General → **Update CLAUDE.md** button; (3) README copy-paste. API: `GET /api/ai-instructions/status` + `POST /api/ai-instructions/apply` (`src/routes/aiInstructions.ts`, typed in `src/api/aiInstructions.ts`). Hot Sheet ships **no** per-language tooling detection — that's delegated to the reading agent via the self-healing block. Tests: `src/aiInstructions.test.ts` (14), `src/client/aiInstructionsNudge.test.ts` (9), `e2e/ai-instructions.spec.ts`.

## 85. Telemetry Retention Bounding (`85-telemetry-retention-bounding.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8888 + HS-8889 + HS-8890, 2026-06-19).** Filed HS-8886 from the HS-8882 bloat investigation; the disk-reclaim half shipped first (**HS-8884** VACUUM pass + **HS-8885** migration move-not-copy, see §67.6). Bounds *row growth within a long-lived session*: (1) **diagnostic** (HS-8888, `src/db/telemetryDiagnostics.ts`) — `telemetryTableBreakdown` per-table row counts + cluster size on `GET /api/telemetry/_debug` (`tableBreakdown`) + an off-loop per-DB startup log (`scheduleTelemetryBreakdownLog`); (2) **periodic 24 h sweep** (HS-8889, `src/telemetryRetentionTimer.ts`) — an `unref`'d timer submitting one coalesced `telemetry-retention-sweep` job (§75, GC, `deferUnderLag`) that runs `cleanupAllProjectsTelemetry` + nudges the vacuum, stopped in `gracefulShutdown`; (3) **per-table windows + span cap** (HS-8890, `src/cleanup.ts`) — `otel_spans` use a 7-day default (`telemetry_span_retention_days` / `centralSpanRetentionDays`) vs 30 d for metrics/events, each `0`=forever, plus `capSpanRows` trimming `otel_spans` to its newest `SPAN_ROW_CAP` (500k) as a burst backstop. Decided HS-8886 design choices: 24 h cadence, span-targeted row cap, spans 7 d.

## 84. Command Button "Last Run" Hover (`84-command-last-run.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8398 + HS-8847 styled tooltip, 2026-06-17).** Hovering a custom command button shows a **styled tooltip** (HS-8847 — a `pointer-events:none` singleton `.command-tooltip` in `src/client/commandTooltip.tsx`, placed beside the button, flips at the viewport edge; replaced the original native `title`) with the command name, its command text, and `Last run: <relative time>` (or `Not run yet`), computed on `mouseenter` via `formatRelativeTime` so it's fresh each hover. "Run" = a shell inline run, a shell run-in-new-terminal (§83.1), or a Claude channel trigger; long-pressing a Claude button to *make a ticket* (§83.2) is NOT a run. Last-run times are recorded **at the click/run site** keyed by the `${secret}::${commandKey}` composite (`runningKey`) — recording at the run site (not deriving from the §14 command log) is what makes it work uniformly for shell AND Claude (the log can't reliably attribute a row to a specific button). Storage: a per-device `localStorage` JSON map (`hotsheet:command-last-run`) in `src/client/commandRunTimes.ts` (`recordCommandRun` / `getCommandLastRun`), zero server cost, corrupt-tolerant. Tests: 7 unit cases for the store + 5 for the tooltip (`commandTooltip.test.ts`). **Cross-device sync (HS-8846) was considered and deliberately declined** — the user confirmed it isn't needed (last-run is a lightweight per-device hint; cross-machine sync isn't cleanly achievable anyway since each server's data is a local gitignored `.hotsheet/`).

## 83. Command-Button Long-Press Actions (`83-command-button-long-press.md`)

**Status: Shipped — §83.1 shell→new-terminal (HS-8539) + §83.2 Claude→Task ticket (HS-8538), both 2026-06-17.** Custom command buttons gain a press-and-hold (≥500 ms) secondary gesture. **§83.1 (shipped):** long-pressing a *shell* command button opens a **new drawer terminal running the user's default shell** and runs the command in it as if typed (shell stays open afterward) — always available regardless of the per-command option. Mechanism: `POST /api/terminal/create` gained an optional `runCommand` (`CreateTerminalReqSchema`); the route eager-spawns the **default shell** (NOT the command as the PTY program) and injects `runCommand\n` via `writeInput` **once the shell output settles** (HS-8840 — `injectCommandWhenSettled` polls `getLastOutputAtMs`: inject after the prompt renders + 150 ms quiet, with a 3 s `maxWaitMs` fallback; adapts to slow shells like PowerShell instead of a fixed 300 ms); output is captured in the ring buffer + replayed on attach. Client: `openTerminalRunningCommand(command, name?)` (`terminal.tsx`) + new `openDrawerTab(tab)` (`commandLog.tsx`); `wireShellButtonPress` (`commandSidebar.tsx`) does the pointerdown timer + click branching + click-suppression-after-long-press. New per-command **`CustomCommand.launchInNewTerminal`** (default off; shell-only checkbox in `commandEditor.tsx`) makes a *normal click* also open a new terminal. **Option B (user's choice):** long-press is *always* new-terminal — when `launchInNewTerminal` is on, click and long-press do the same thing (not an inverse). One-time first-use hint toast on the first *normal click* of any shell button (`localStorage` `hotsheet:shell-longpress-hint-shown`). Tests: server route `runCommand` injection (fake-timers + write-capturing PTY factory in `api.test.ts`); `e2e/command-long-press.spec.ts` (HS-8839/HS-8844) drives a real press-and-hold past the 500 ms threshold and asserts the shell gesture opens a `terminal:dyn-*` tab + the Claude gesture creates a `task` ticket (skips when the sidebar/Claude button can't render); per-OS default-shell + first-use toasts stay manual-test items. **§83.2 (shipped, HS-8538):** long-press a *Claude* button → `wireClaudeButtonPress` calls `makeTaskFromClaudeCommand` → `createTicket({ title: cmd.name, defaults: { category: 'task', details: cmd.prompt } })` + reload; category is always `task` (TSK) and works even if `task` isn't in the project's configured categories (free-string column). One-time first-click hint toast (`hotsheet:claude-longpress-hint-shown`); the connect-failure `window.alert` was replaced with a warning toast. Gesture covered by `e2e/command-long-press.spec.ts` (HS-8844).

## 82. Announcer Mid-task Narration (`82-announcer-mid-task-narration.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8789, 2026-06-06).** Makes live mode (§80) narrate work **as it happens** by adding the §67 telemetry event stream as a signal source, with the AI rating importance and dropping the uninteresting. New `src/announcer/telemetrySignals.ts::collectTelemetrySignals(projectSecret, since)` reads `user_prompt` + `tool_result` from the shared telemetry DB and renders a few lines **grouped by user-prompt turn** ("[in progress] working on: \"<snippet>\" (used Bash ×3, Edit ×2)"; marker-stripped, 200-char snippet; an orphan-tool catch-all; 30 min look-back when no cursor). `collectWorkSignals(since, {projectSecret, includeTelemetry})` merges them under the same cap. **Triggering:** the OTLP receiver (`routes/otel.ts`) calls `notifyChange()` after a metrics/logs ingest with `inserted>0` so the live loop wakes on telemetry; the live `CoalescingTrigger` quiet window is now **15 s** (max-wait 30 s) per the user, coalescing a turn's burst (governs the whole shared live loop). **Importance:** `EntrySchema` + the Anthropic `output_config` + the local prompt carry `importance` low|medium|high; `dropUnimportant()` filters `low` on all provider paths before persist (only explicit `low` dropped, so Apple's schema-less entries survive); the system prompt marks routine/in-progress churn `low` and completed work medium/high. **Gating:** telemetry included only when the live generator passes `includeTelemetry:true` AND the project's `telemetry_enabled !== false`; never on the manual after-the-fact generate. Budget (HS-8770 callBudget) + off-unless-listening lease unchanged; spend on §70/§71 via `announcer_usage`. Tests: `telemetrySignals.test.ts`, `collectSignals.test.ts` (merge gating), `summarize.test.ts` (low-importance drop). Follow-ups: prompt tuning if the global low-filter over-drops the after-the-fact digest; a per-project "don't send prompt text" privacy toggle; real-data manual validation.

## 81. Announcer Local Provider (`81-announcer-local-provider.md`)

**Status: Shipped (HS-8792, 2026-06-06).** A cross-platform, free/private, on-device Announcer summarization provider that talks to a **user-run local LLM over the OpenAI-compatible HTTP API** (Ollama / LM Studio / llama.cpp / vLLM) — the Linux/older-Mac/non-Copilot-Windows counterpart to macOS-only Apple Foundation Models (§78 / HS-8790). Slots into the provider-tagged registry: `models.ts` adds provider `'local'` + pseudo-id `LOCAL_MODEL_ID` ($0 pricing); `src/announcer/localProvider.ts` probes `{base}/models` (reachable + ≥1 model ⇒ available, 10 s TTL cache), lists installed models, and POSTs `{base}/chat/completions`; `summarize.ts` routes `local` → `runLocalSummarize` with an appended explicit-JSON instruction (no output-schema enforcement on a generic model) + tolerant `parseEntriesJson`, `usage: null`. Config: global `announcerLocalEndpoint` (default `http://localhost:11434/v1`) + `announcerLocalModel`. A new shared `prepareSummarizationProvider(model)` in `generate.ts` is the single gating SSOT (anthropic key / apple helper / local endpoint) used by the generate route, the live-lease gate, and the live generator (replaced the duplicated per-site branching). `/overview` adds `localAvailable`; `/status` adds `localAvailable` + `localModels`. Settings → Announcer shows the "Local model" option only when available; selecting it reveals an endpoint URL field + a **dropdown of detected models** and hides the Anthropic key field. Tests: `localProvider.test.ts` (availability matrix, model parse, TTL cache, endpoint resolution, chat call), `summarize.test.ts` (local routing), `models.test.ts` (provider + $0). Follow-ups: e2e for the settings dropdown; mid-task narration is the separate HS-8789.

## 65. Read Latest Note context-menu item (`65-read-latest-note-menu.md`)

HS-8401 (shipped 2026-05-15). A right-click affordance on ticket rows + column-view cards that surfaces a **Read Latest Note** item with the Lucide `book-open-text` icon, opening the most recent non-empty note in the §49 reader overlay. Single entry-point that collapses today's "select ticket → scroll to note → hover row → click book icon" flow into one right-click. Lives in `showTicketContextMenu` (`src/client/contextMenu.tsx`) and therefore appears on both list-view rows and column-view cards without per-surface wiring.

**Behavior.** Single-selection only (`state.selectedIds.size === 1`); omitted on multi-select since the reader targets one note. **HS-8841 — description fallback:** when the ticket has no non-empty note the item falls back to reading the **Details** (relabeled "Read Description") and is disabled (greyed-out, present) ONLY when there's neither a non-empty note nor a description (precedence: latest note → description → disabled). A note counts as "empty" when its `text.trim() === ''`; the search walks the notes array from the end to find the most recent non-empty entry, so a placeholder note at the top doesn't hide an older real one. Opens `openReaderOverlay({ title: buildNoteReaderTitle(note.created_at), markdown: note.text })`; the overlay's own dismiss / Esc / backdrop-click behavior is unchanged from §49.

**Implementation.** Pure helper `findLatestNonEmptyNote(notesJson)` returns `{ text, created_at } | null`. `addActionItem(menu, label, action, { icon, disabled })` was widened with a `disabled?: boolean` option that applies `.disabled` and skips click-listener attachment. Six unit tests in `src/client/contextMenu.test.ts` under `showTicketContextMenu — Read Latest Note (HS-8401)` cover the enabled / disabled / placeholder-only / latest-non-empty-search / older-non-empty-when-newer-empty / multi-select-omit cases.

**Status:** Shipped 2026-05-15. Cross-refs: §49 (reader overlay), §59 (reader-note navigation buttons — orthogonal; the menu item opens a single-entry overlay without navigation chevrons since the request is "the latest note" specifically).

## 64. Auto-allow Hot Sheet MCP tools in `.claude/settings.local.json` (`64-claude-allow-rule.md`)

HS-8376 design + HS-8377 implementation. Companion to §63's MCP tool surface + HS-8349's per-project server naming. When a Hot Sheet project's `.claude/` directory exists, `registerChannel(dataDir)` also writes the wildcard rule `mcp__hotsheet-channel-<slug>__*` into `.claude/settings.local.json`'s `permissions.allow` array so Claude Code accepts every `hotsheet_*` MCP tool call without per-call permission prompts. The slug is `slugifyDataDir(dataDir)` (HS-8349) — wildcard support in Claude Code's allow rules only kicks in after the second `__`, so the slug must be embedded into the pattern.

**Decisions** (full table in §64.2): piggyback on `registerChannel` (D1), symmetric removal on `unregisterChannel` (D2), create `.claude/settings.local.json` when `.claude/` exists but the file doesn't (D3), skip when `.claude/` is absent (D4), idempotent + non-reformatting + non-reordering writes (D5), failure-open on parse / write errors (D6), per-project opt-out via `claude_auto_allow_rule: false` in `<dataDir>/settings.json` (D7, default `true`).

**Implementation (HS-8377, shipped 2026-05-13).** New `src/claude-allow-rule.ts` exports `syncClaudeAllowRule(dataDir)` + `unsyncClaudeAllowRule(dataDir)` + `claudeAllowRulePattern(dataDir)`. `src/channel-config.ts::registerChannel` calls `syncClaudeAllowRule(dataDir)` after the `.mcp.json` write; `unregisterChannel(dataDir)` calls `unsyncClaudeAllowRule(dataDir)` after the `.mcp.json` cleanup (only on the dataDir-known path — the no-arg legacy stale-cleanup branch leaves the file alone since it can't resolve the slug). The opt-out is read via the existing `readFileSettings(dataDir)`; default-on for the missing-key path. **18 unit tests** in `src/claude-allow-rule.test.ts` cover every §64.4 case (`.claude/` absent / present-without-file / present-with-file / rule-already-present / other-entries-preserved / other-keys-preserved / malformed-json-warns-and-leaves-alone / opt-out / explicit-on / multi-project-parity / 2-space-indent-plus-trailing-newline for both sync and unsync). **4 integration tests** in `src/channel-config.test.ts` under a new `register/unregisterChannel × claude-allow-rule integration (HS-8377)` describe block cover the cross-file behaviors: `registerChannel` writes both, `registerChannel` writes only `.mcp.json` when `.claude/` is absent, `unregisterChannel` removes from both, and the `claude_auto_allow_rule: false` opt-out suppresses the `.claude/` write path while still writing `.mcp.json`. No `CHANNEL_VERSION` bump — `.mcp.json` semantics unchanged.

**Status:** Shipped 2026-05-13 (design + implementation in the same session). Cross-refs: §12 (channel lifecycle, `.mcp.json`), §63 (the MCP tool surface this unlocks), HS-8349 (slug-suffix server naming).

## 57. Shell custom-command-button spinner & stop (`57-shell-command-button-spinner.md`)

HS-8056 (spec) + HS-8060 (Phase 1 implementation, shipped 2026-05-01). When a §15 Shell-target custom-command button is running, the button itself surfaces an absolute-positioned spinner + stop icon at the right edge (`background: inherit` so it visually punches the button color, no reflow against the label). Clicking the running button opens a `confirmDialog` → `POST /api/shell/kill`. Multiple commands can run simultaneously; per-button state lives in a module-private `runningButtons: Map<commandKey, logId>` synced by a single shared poll over `/api/shell/running` (replacing the pre-fix single-id-per-timer model). The existing global "Shell running" toolbar indicator now reflects `runningButtons.size > 0` (busy = any button running). Per-id `autoShowLogById` map replaces the global `shellAutoShowLog: boolean` so concurrent commands' auto-show flags don't clobber each other.

**Status:** Shipped (Phase 1).

**Cross-refs.** §15 (shell-commands base flow + the existing `/api/shell/exec`+`/api/shell/kill`+`/api/shell/running` endpoints), §53 (streaming output — orthogonal; the spinner doesn't subscribe to the partial-output stream).
